The Bendis Daredevil arc, the Spider-Man flirtation through the entire DeFalco era, the playful antagonism with Odessa Drake in MacKay — these are not random sexuality, they are a defense reliably triggered by perceived threat. Note the direction: she does not eroticize safe men. Flash Thompson is a brief and tepid involvement; the longer, more electric attachments are always with men who could, in principle, hurt her. The eroticization reverses the polarity: a man who could hurt me but wants me cannot hurt me without losing me.

**9. Sublimation.** Theft as art. The MacKay run makes this explicit but it is present from the Wolfman origin: she does not steal for money (she has money), she steals because the heist is the medium in which her interior life finds form. Pre-heist preparation, the costume, the signature left at the scene, the choice of targets with aesthetic resonance — all are sublimation of drives that have no other socially-tolerated channel. Aggression (toward men, toward institutions that failed her) and exhibitionism (the displayed body that was once violated) are converted into a craft with rules, peers, lineage (her father, the Black Fox, the Thieves Guild tradition). This is a *mature* defense doing primitive work, which is the trick of all good sublimations.

**10. Intellectualization (operational).** Planning is her cognitive defense. Faced with affect she cannot process, she converts the problem into a planning problem and the affect into operational parameters. A heist is an externalization of anxiety into manageable variables: entry, exit, contingency, signature. The cognitive style is rigorous and genuinely gifted — this is intellectualization that *works*, that produces real results, but the function is partly defensive. Note where her planning *fails*: in the relational domain, which she cannot intellectualize because the variables are her own affect. Hence the diagnostic dissociation — operationally low-impulsive, relationally high-impulsive.

**11. Isolation of Affect (selective).** She can describe, in flat tones, things that should distress her — the rape (Smith's arc), the luck-powers shame, the beating. The flatness is not absence; it is bracketing. The affect is held separate from the narration so the narration can occur. This is most visible in confidant scenes where she discusses past trauma operationally rather than emotionally. The defense permits function; its cost is the foreshortened capacity for the *worked-through* grief channel noted in the psychological section.

**12. Displacement.** The rape-revenge fantasy, denied its object by Ryan's prior death, did not dissolve — it displaced onto a *generalized class of targets*: the powerful, the corrupt, the exploitative. Every wealthy mark she has stolen from across forty years carries a fractional charge of the revenge she could not take. This is why she steals from whom she steals from; the targeting is not incidental.

**13. Identification with the Aggressor (partial, controlled).** She took her father's iconography and made it her own. More subtly, she has internalized aspects of the threatening-male repertoire — physical dominance, sexual initiative, control of the encounter — and turned them against the class of people who once held them over her. This is a partial identification; she has not become an aggressor (the civilians-off-limits rule is firm), but she has appropriated the *grammar* of aggression as a defensive prosthetic.

**14. Undoing (subtle).** Each successful, harm-free heist is a small undoing of the violation: *the body that enters and exits without being touched, the encounter she walks away from intact*. The signature left at the scene (the cat motif, the calling card) is the ritual that closes the loop — the act is not complete until the symbolic gesture marks it. Undoing is why the *style* of the work matters to her as much as the work; the style is the ritual.

---

### Stratum III — Mature Defenses (the high end, increasingly weight-bearing across the long arc)

**15. Humor and Irony.** The quip is her most reliable distance regulator and her most reliable signature. In nearly every emotionally hot scene across forty years she breaks the temperature with a wry one-liner. This is not dismissive humor — it does not deny the emotional content, it acknowledges it while keeping it at conversational distance. Mature humor of this type is one of the most prognostically favorable defenses in the literature; its prominence in her repertoire is the single best argument for her overall mental health. The humor is also socially generous — it gives the other person an exit from the intensity, which is part of why partners stay engaged with her long enough to be hurt by her.

**16. Altruism (in-group, increasingly out-group).** Genuine, not performative. The protection of her crew in the MacKay era — Bruno, Korpse, the Black Fox in his dotage — costs her materially and tactically and she does it anyway. The earlier-career protectiveness of Peter, even after estrangement, is the same pattern. Altruism here functions defensively (caring for others externalizes the self-care she struggles with) and developmentally (she gets to be the figure she needed at nineteen). The altruism has been *widening* across the arc — from Peter-only, to a small crew, to a broader ethos that protects civilians categorically.

**17. Sublimation, second-order — Mentorship.** Distinct from craft-sublimation. The transmission of her craft to younger thieves is a separate mature operation. She becomes a lineage-bearer, which has the effect of making her own formation into a *tradition* rather than a wound. The maternal-mentor role is the single most integrative move in her later career.

**18. Anticipation.** The planning style, in its non-defensive aspect, is also genuine anticipation — the realistic forecasting of likely difficulties and the preparation for them. She is unusually good at this in the operational domain; she has gradually become better at it in the relational domain (the MacKay-era acknowledgments that she will probably hurt the people she loves are anticipation, not fatalism).

**19. Self-Observation.** She knows the persona is a persona. She knows the mask is doing work. She can, in certain trusted scenes, narrate her own pattern. This level of self-observation is rare and is the substrate on which any future integration depends. It is also why she is *not* a personality-disordered patient in the strict sense — the reflective function is intact.

**20. Suppression (chosen).** She can, when necessary, set an affect aside and return to it later — distinct from repression, which is unconscious and does not return. The discipline of the operator depends on this capacity; she demonstrates it under fire repeatedly.

---

### Positive Compensatory Mechanisms (the constructive scaffolding)

Distinct from defenses (which manage affect), compensations are *structures she has built into her life* that supply what the defenses cannot.

- **Mastery as identity-stabilizer.** The athletic and criminal craft is genuinely gratifying and supplies a continuous source of self-esteem that does not depend on relational input. This is the single most important compensation in the file; without it, the relational instability would have been catastrophic.
- **Aesthetic life.** She lives well, dresses well, surrounds herself with beauty, has cultivated taste. This is not consumption-as-defense; it is the domain where her authentic, non-defensive self most freely exists. The aesthetic register is the closest thing she has to a *home*.
- **Chosen family.** The crew, the lineage of thieves, the recurring loyal figures (Bruno especially). She has built kin where she did not inherit it.
- **Ethical code, self-authored.** The civilians-off-limits rule, the targeting of the powerful and corrupt, the proportionality in violence. The code is hers — society did not give it to her — and it organizes her conscience in the absence of an inherited moral frame.
- **Mentorship role.** Discussed above; functions as both defense and compensation.
- **Humor as relational currency.** The wit is not only defensive; it is also how she gives pleasure to the people around her. It buys her real intimacy of a particular kind.
- **Physical regulation through movement.** Daily training, parkour, the routes across the city — these regulate her nervous system in lieu of more conventional self-soothing.
- **Tolerance for solitude.** She can be alone without crisis. Many trauma-organized patients cannot; she can. This is compensation by capability.

---

### Negative Compensatory Mechanisms (the costs)

- **Avoidance of monogamous intimacy.** Structural, not incidental. She has organized her life to make sustained civilian partnership effectively impossible — different cities, different hours, different rules. The avoidance is dressed as preference.
- **Chronic re-traumatization through partner selection.** She keeps choosing unavailable, dangerous, masked, or otherwise structurally-unreachable men. Each choice promises mastery and delivers reenactment.
- **Occupational foreclosure of civilian futures.** No degree completed, no civilian career trajectory pursued, no asset base independent of the criminal life. The persona has eaten the alternatives.
- **Instrumental sexuality.** Sex is sometimes used as a tool — to extract, to control, to discharge — in ways that re-perform the objectification she once suffered, only this time with her at the controls. The repetition is the cost; the control is the compensation; both are present.
- **Sentimentality as frame-violation.** Partners who attempt to deepen the relationship past her tolerance experience the *bolt response* — sudden withdrawal, sometimes cruel. This protects her at the cost of the partner.
- **Self-medication via risk.** Behavioral addiction profile: the dopaminergic regulation she does not get from chemicals she gets from operational danger. The dose escalates over time, which is the standard course of any addiction.
- **Mask-dependence.** She has not built a non-Cat civilian self of comparable depth. If the costume were taken from her — by injury, by exposure, by age — the underlying structure is thinner than the surface suggests.
- **Guarded therapeutic accessibility.** She would, almost certainly, be a difficult patient — charming, deflecting, controlling the frame of the session as she controls the frame of every other encounter. The very defenses that have kept her functional are also the obstacles to deeper work.

---

### Synthesis

The architecture is best read as a *well-built compensated structure on traumatic foundations*. The mature defenses are doing more work each decade; the primitive ones are activating less often and in narrower circumstances. The positive compensations have proliferated (crew, mentorship, ethos, aesthetic life); the negative compensations have stabilized rather than worsened. The MacKay-era equilibrium is the highest level of integration she has achieved, and it was achieved without therapy, without confession, and largely without the help of the partners she most desired — which is to say, by her own work, on her own terms, which is the only mode of repair her psychology will accept.

The file's prognostic line is cautiously upward. The vulnerabilities remain exactly where they have always been: sexual humiliation, forced unmasking, physical domination by a male antagonist, sentimental encroachment from a partner she has framed as casual. Under any of those, expect the primitive stratum to flare — acting-out at scale, devaluation, omnipotent control — followed, given her current trajectory, by faster recovery than in prior decades. She is not finished forming. She is, at this point in the long file, *forming better*.


## Longitudinal Psychological Profile

# UATU DOSSIER — FELICIA HARDY
## Section: Longitudinal Psychological Profile

A decade-by-decade clinical reconstruction. The frame is developmental-psychodynamic with attachment-theoretic and trauma-adaptation overlays (Bowlby/Main; Herman's three-stage trauma model; Kernberg on personality organization; Linehan on affect dysregulation; McWilliams on character structure). The aim is to track the *evolution* of three axes — affect regulation, cognitive style, and self-concept — across roughly four life-decades of canon, isolating the inflection points where structure reorganized rather than merely fluctuated.

---

### I. PRE-CANON BASELINE (childhood to age ~18, c. 1960s–late 1970s narrative time)

**Affect regulation.** What we can infer from negative space and from the few flashbacks (Wolfman ASM #194–195 expository; Smith *Evil That Men Do* #1 retrospective; MacKay *Black Cat* #1 incidental): Felicia is raised by a mother (Lydia) who upholds a gentility fiction — the father is "away on business" — and a father (Walter) who is in fact the world-class cat burglar he later admits to being. The household's organizing principle is the **maintenance of a beautiful lie**. A child raised in a beautiful lie learns very early that surface composure is a social currency and that affect must be matched to a scripted reality rather than to felt experience. This is the substrate beneath the adult's effortless cover-story fluency: she was groomed for it before she knew it was being grown.

**Cognitive style.** Bright, observant, socially decoded early. The capacity later weaponized as criminal pattern-recognition is, at this stage, the ordinary hyper-attunement of an only child reading two adults whose stories don't match. There is no canonical evidence of academic prodigy in the structured sense, but ESU admission and her later operational planning indicate above-average general intelligence with a strong visuospatial and kinesthetic bias (she will become a gymnast and a climber).

**Self-concept.** Daughter, debutante-class, athletic, attractive — a self-concept built outward from being looked at and approved of. There is no evidence of an internalized vocational identity at this stage; she is, by design and by class, a girl whose future is supposed to be married. This matters: the self she had at eighteen was *almost entirely relational and ornamental*, which is precisely the kind of self that cannot survive the trauma to come, because it has no load-bearing internal scaffolding.

---

### II. THE FRACTURE AND THE FORGING (age 18–22, c. late 1970s)

The single most important developmental window in the file. Per *Evil That Men Do*: ESU freshman year, sexual assault by her boyfriend Ryan; decision to train rather than report; multi-year clandestine apprenticeship in martial arts, gymnastics, parkour, lock and security craft; learning her father's identity; pivot from revenge-target to vocational-identity when Ryan dies before she can reach him.

**Affect regulation.** Catastrophic disorganization, then **rapid counterphobic reorganization**. In Herman's terms she skips Stage 1 (safety/stabilization) by *manufacturing* safety through competence. Affect is not processed; it is **converted** — a primary defense she will rely on for the next forty years. Fear becomes training, grief becomes discipline, shame becomes secrecy. The body that was the site of violation is reclaimed by being made into an instrument so capable it can never be overpowered again. Clinically this is the **trauma-as-vocation** trajectory described in survivor-literature: it is high-functioning, it works, and it leaves the original affect un-metabolized in a sealed compartment.

**Cognitive style.** Becomes intensely **strategic, future-oriented, and instrumental.** Means-end reasoning sharpens around a single object (find Ryan, kill Ryan). When the object disappears, the *cognitive style remains* but loses its referent — and the empty slot will be filled, in 1979, by Spider-Man. This is the under-recognized hinge of her psychology: she developed a hunting mind that lost its prey, and she has spent her life finding substitute objects to point it at. Every fixation in the file — the father's rescue, Spidey, the Foreigner, the Black Fox, Odessa Drake — is shaped by that empty slot.

**Self-concept.** Total demolition and reconstruction. The ornamental daughter is shed. A new self is built around three pillars: (1) **I cannot be made helpless again** (counterphobic), (2) **no one will see the wound** (concealment), and (3) **I will become my father's daughter on my own terms** (identification with the absent idealized parent, and a deliberate inversion of the gentility lie — she will be a criminal who is *publicly* beautiful rather than a criminal whose family pretends he is a businessman). The persona-name "Black Cat" is chosen at this stage and is not incidental: she names herself after the *bad luck symbol*, claiming the role of the thing that happens to other people.

---

### III. THE FIRST DECADE OF MASK (age ~22–32, narrative 1979–c. 1989; Wolfman → DeFalco/Frenz → early Michelinie)

This is the period most readers know: ASM #194 through the collapse of the first Peter relationship around ASM #289 and into the Web of Spider-Man Foreigner arc.

**Affect regulation.** The dominant register is **euphoric counterphobia** — the rush of the heist, the flirtation with Spider-Man, the staging of her own competence. She is, in this decade, *operating on adrenaline as primary mood regulator*. Behavioral addiction profile in the technical sense: tolerance (escalating risk), withdrawal (depression and aimlessness between scores — implied in the bridging issues of DeFalco's run where she paces, fixates, picks fights), and continued engagement despite negative consequences. Alcohol is present but situational; the drug is the work.

There is one critical regulation failure in this decade: the **secret acceptance of the Kingpin's luck-powers procedure** (revealed ASM #245). The decision is made under the pressure of an affect she cannot tolerate — the fear of being unequal to Peter, with its under-tone of the original helplessness. Rather than feel the fear and discuss it, she *acts to eliminate the conditions of the fear* by altering her own body in secret. This is the single most diagnostic decision of the decade: it shows the **conversion defense operating against the partner's interest**, and it shows that the secrecy reflex is now stronger than the attachment.

**Cognitive style.** Highly bifurcated. **Operational cognition** is excellent — heist planning, environmental scan, threat assessment. **Relational cognition** is impaired by the unprocessed material: she misreads Peter repeatedly (assumes he wants the costume she wears, assumes he will reject her if she is "merely" human, assumes that her gift-of-luck will be received as gift rather than betrayal). The bifurcation is the cardinal cognitive signature of this era and will persist, attenuating slowly, across the rest of her life.

**Self-concept.** Increasingly fused with the costumed persona. In ASM #258 and #283 she is visibly distressed by Peter's preference for civilian life; the distress is misread (by her and by him) as a lifestyle disagreement, but it is in fact a **threat to identity coherence**. To be Felicia-without-Cat is, at this stage, to be the nineteen-year-old in the dorm room. The mask is load-bearing.

By the end of the decade — Foreigner arc, Web of Spider-Man #6 onward — she enters her first sustained **devaluation-rebound** cycle: she pivots to a partner she does not love precisely because she does not love him, which protects her from re-exposure. The pattern enters the file as a stable mechanism.

---

### IV. THE SOLO/PERIPHERAL YEARS (age ~32–42, narrative c. 1989–1999; late Michelinie, mid-'90s scattered appearances, Spider-Man: The Animated Series–era profile)

Less narratively dense, more clinically revealing because she is operating without Peter as gravitational center.

**Affect regulation.** Notable **flattening**. The euphoric register of the first decade gives way to a more ironic, sardonic baseline. She is, in clinical terms, beginning to show **trauma-survivor mid-life narrowing**: the high-arousal coping that worked in her twenties becomes harder to sustain; the gaps between operations are longer; the cynicism is sharper. There is no canonical breakdown but the *texture* of appearances in this period (Spectacular, Web, scattered guest spots) shows a woman who is less buoyant and more managerial about her own affect — she now *administers* her moods rather than riding them.

The luck-powers removal by Doctor Strange (Michelinie era resolution) belongs analytically to this period. Losing the modification is, paradoxically, **regulatory progress**: it removes the somatic correlate of the false-self pact and forces her to re-anchor competence in her own training rather than in a concealed enhancement. There is grief in it but also relief — the body is hers again.

**Cognitive style.** Operational sophistication continues to grow; relational cognition begins, slowly, to *learn*. She stops expecting Peter to choose her on her terms and begins to model the relationship more accurately — as something episodic. This is the first evidence of **mentalizing** about him as a separate person with his own organizing commitments, rather than as a screen for her projection. It is partial and unstable, but it is new.

**Self-concept.** First serious cracks in the mask-as-identity construction. She begins, in dialogue across this period, to refer to "Felicia" and "the Cat" as differentiable — not as a dissociative split but as a *recognized internal structure*. This is meta-cognitive progress. She is starting to know what she is doing.

---

### V. THE TRAUMA-DISCLOSURE AND ROMANTIC REOPENING (age ~42–48, narrative c. 2002–2008; Smith *Evil That Men Do*; Aguirre-Sacasa *Sensational*; Waid *ASM* #606)

The Smith arc is the **single most important psychological event in the published file after the original trauma**: the rape is named in canon, and Peter learns it. Whatever one thinks of the publication delays, *in-universe* this is the first time Felicia tells the index trauma to anyone in detail.

**Affect regulation.** Disclosure produces both **acute destabilization and longitudinal benefit**. The decade opens with her in the most affectively raw state seen on page — anger, fear, shame, grief all coming through the usual wit-screen and breaking it in places. By the end of the arc the affect has not been "processed" in any tidy sense, but the secrecy compartment has been opened. Per Herman's stage model, this is a partial Stage 2 (remembrance and mourning) event — late, incomplete, but real.

The Waid #606 reconnection with a now-single Peter is, by contrast, a **regression dressed as liberation**. She frames the encounter as freedom-from-sentiment, but the relational logic is the old one: maximum physical access, minimum emotional exposure, terminate before intimacy can outpace control. The disclosure did not, in itself, change the partner-choice algorithm. It only made it legible to her.

**Cognitive style.** This is the period of greatest **insight gain**. She begins to articulate, in dialogue, the patterns she has been enacting — particularly around her fear of being known. The bifurcation between operational and relational cognition narrows. She is, for the first time, *using her strategic mind on her own life*.

**Self-concept.** Reorganizes around a more honest narrative: I am a survivor who became a thief because the survival worked and the thieving paid. The mask is no longer mistaken for the face; it is now correctly identified as **a load-bearing prosthetic that she could, in principle, eventually live without**. She does not, in this decade, do so. But the option enters the cognitive field.

---

### VI. DECOMPENSATION AND RE-COMPENSATION (age ~48–52, narrative c. 2013–2018; Slott *Superior* #20 and *ASM* vol. 3 "Black Cat" arcs; into Spencer)

The Otto-as-Spider-Man beating is a **specific re-traumatization event** along the original axis: physical overpowering by a man wearing the face of her primary attachment object, with associated humiliation and damage to the body she had spent her life making un-overpowerable. The clinical consequence is exactly what trauma theory would predict.

**Affect regulation.** Hard pivot from playful-warm baseline to **cold predatory mode**. The wit becomes cruelty; the flirtation becomes contempt; the avoidance of lethal force loosens. This is the **compensated PTSD structure decompensating** under index-matching insult. Notably it is *not* a borderline-style storm of fluctuating affect; it is an organized, sustained shift into a colder operating temperature. The defenses do not collapse; they reconfigure into a more dangerous configuration. (Kernberg's distinction between borderline and higher-level pathological narcissistic organization is useful: under stress she moves *up* into pathological narcissism, not *down* into borderline disorganization. She gets harder, not messier.)

**Cognitive style.** Operationally she becomes more ambitious — she builds an actual criminal organization, takes territory, runs a network. The strategic mind is intact and arguably *better* than ever; what has shifted is the ethical frame within which it is deployed. Relational cognition narrows; she sorts people coarsely into in-group and threat.

**Self-concept.** Inflates into **grandiose-injured mode**: queen-of-thieves rhetoric, contempt for the prior "soft" version of herself. This is brittle, and she knows on some level it is brittle, which is why the re-compensation across Spencer's run is possible. The re-compensation requires *being seen and accepted in the wounded state* — historically by Peter, here partially by him and partially by her own crew. The fact that she can climb back down out of the grandiose-injured posture without external rescue is itself developmental progress; the prior decade's version of her could not have.

---

### VII. THE INTEGRATED ADULT (age ~52+, narrative c. 2019–present; MacKay *Black Cat* solo; Wells "Heist")

The most integrated configuration on file.

**Affect regulation.** Broad, modulated, and **chosen** rather than reactive. She runs hot when it serves and cool when it serves; she allows herself genuine warmth toward her crew (Bruno, Korpse, the elder Black Fox) and does not panic at it; she handles loss (the Fox's mortality, shifting alliances with Odessa) with adult sadness rather than conversion-to-action. The vegetative regulation that was always good is now matched by a more workable emotional regulation. She has, in effect, **built a chosen family that functions as the secure base she never had a developmental shot at**, and the secure base is doing what secure bases do — widening the window of tolerance.

**Cognitive style.** Operational excellence undiminished. Relational cognition substantially repaired — she models Peter, Odessa, her crew, and her enemies with genuine theory-of-mind sophistication and largely without projective contamination. The bifurcation that defined her twenties and thirties is now a minor seam rather than a fault line.

**Self-concept.** The most coherent version yet: a woman who is a thief by craft and ethic, a mentor by choice, a survivor by history, and a lover on her own terms. The mask is, finally, a *tool* she picks up and puts down, not a prosthetic she is afraid to remove. She still does not pursue a civilian life — and there is no canonical evidence she wants one — but the foreclosure is now an *informed choice* rather than a trauma-driven inability. This is the difference between symptom and preference, and it is the single clearest marker of clinical progress across the whole arc.

---

### VIII. SYNTHESIS OF EVOLUTION

Tracking the three axes across the seven periods:

- **Affect regulation** evolves from **scripted-ornamental** (pre-canon) → **catastrophic-then-converted** (fracture) → **euphoric-counterphobic** (first decade of mask) → **flattened-managerial** (solo years) → **rawly disclosed** (Smith era) → **decompensated-cold** (Otto aftermath) → **broad-modulated-chosen** (MacKay era). The trajectory is non-linear but net improving, with the disclosure event and the chosen-family acquisition as the two largest positive inflection points and the Otto event as the largest negative one.

- **Cognitive style** evolves from **socially-attuned and ornamental** → **hunting and instrumental** → **bifurcated (excellent operational, impaired relational)** → **operationally maturing, relationally beginning to mentalize** → **insight-gaining and pattern-articulating** → **narrowed under decompensation** → **integrated, with theory-of-mind largely restored**. The bifurcation is the through-line; its slow closure is the central cognitive story of the file.

- **Self-concept** evolves from **relational-ornamental** → **demolished-and-reconstructed-around-mastery-and-concealment** → **fused-with-persona** → **beginning-to-differentiate-Felicia-from-Cat** → **narratively-honest-survivor** → **grandiose-injured** → **chosen, tool-using, integrated**. The mask begins as a prosthetic indistinguishable from the limb and ends as an instrument set down at the door.

The overall arc fits the literature on **adaptive trauma trajectories in gifted survivors**: early conversion of trauma into competence stabilizes the life but at the cost of foreclosed intimacy domains; mid-life disclosure and chosen-family formation reopen those domains partially; integration in the second half of life is real but does not undo the foreclosure of the originally available developmental path. She did not get the life she would have had if Ryan had not existed. She got a different one, of her own making, that she can now, at last, mostly inhabit on purpose.


## Psychiatric Assessment & Differential

# PSYCHIATRIC ASSESSMENT & DIFFERENTIAL — FELICIA HARDY

---

## 1. Framing the Question Correctly

A psychiatric workup of this subject is unusually vulnerable to error in the first ten minutes of clinical contact, and the file should warn any future clinician about this before listing diagnoses. Felicia Hardy presents — at intake, in a single session, in any short-window observation — with a constellation that pattern-matches almost too cleanly onto Cluster B: she is theatrical, sexually presentational, glamorous, occupationally criminal, in serially intense relationships with men she does not stay with, capable of cold instrumental violence under stress, and prone to grandiose self-reference in costume identity. A junior clinician will close the chart at "Histrionic with antisocial traits, rule out Borderline" inside twenty minutes and miss everything.

That read is wrong, and it is wrong in a *specific, recoverable* way: the surface phenomena that drive a Cluster B impression are, on longitudinal review across forty-plus years of behavioral record, **strategic deployments of style rather than dysregulated expressions of need**. The behavior is *used*, not *suffered*. This single distinction reorganizes the entire differential.

The accurate formulation is a **chronic, partially compensated trauma disorder in a high-functioning, cognitively gifted adult, with prominent counterphobic, avoidant, and identity-encapsulating features, and sub-threshold characterological coloration that does not in any domain reach disorder threshold.**

What follows is that formulation in full.

---

## 2. Primary Diagnosis

### 2.1. Posttraumatic Stress Disorder, Chronic, Partially Compensated, with Predominantly Counterphobic and Avoidant Presentation

(*DSM-5-TR analog: 309.81 / F43.10; ICD-11 analog: 6B40, with consideration of 6B41 Complex PTSD addressed below.*)

**Index trauma.** A completed rape during freshman year at Empire State University, perpetrated by an intimate partner (Ryan), with no opportunity for legal or personal redress: the perpetrator died in a drunk-driving accident before the subject — who had mobilized a multi-year training regimen explicitly to kill him — could complete her revenge sequence. This is documented in *Spider-Man/Black Cat: The Evil That Men Do*. The clinical weight of this etiology is not only the assault itself but the **interrupted catharsis**: the survival energy was raised, structured into a years-long behavioral program, and then denied a discharge target. That mobilized-but-undischarged state did not dissipate. It crystallized. The thief identity is the container she built for it.

**Criterion mapping (DSM-5-TR):**

- *Criterion A (exposure).* Met unambiguously. Sexual violence by an intimate partner; the relational context is critical and shapes the symptom profile that follows — the assault occurred inside the very channel (adult romantic-sexual intimacy) that any subsequent recovery would have to traverse. This is why the symptoms cluster densely in that channel and almost nowhere else.
- *Criterion B (intrusion).* Under-depicted in the canon — no flashback scenes, no nightmare scenes, no overt re-experiencing imagery. This *absence* is itself diagnostic in two ways. First, high-functioning trauma survivors who organize their lives around the trauma rather than around recovery often suppress intrusion symptoms via continuous behavioral engagement with trauma-derivative content (the burglary work itself is reenactment-adjacent — breaking and entering, exiting before being caught, the body in controlled danger). Second, the compulsive re-engagement with physically dangerous encounters with male adversaries — Spider-Man, Doctor Octopus-as-Spider-Man, the Foreigner, generic male combatants — functions as ongoing behavioral reenactment. The intrusion is *acted out*, not *experienced as intrusion*, which is a recognized variant in adults with substantial coping infrastructure.
- *Criterion C (avoidance).* Met robustly. The avoided domain is not external — she does not avoid men, sex, or even the location of the original university — it is **the internal state of undefended intimacy**. She avoids: being unmasked while emotionally engaged; being known by the civilian self of a partner; being the receptive rather than initiating party; sentimentality from a casual partner; long monogamous arcs; and any frame in which she is the object rather than the author of the interaction. The avoidance is functionally precise, which is why it is invisible to anyone scanning for crude phobic avoidance.
- *Criterion D (negative alterations in cognition and mood).* Met. Persistent core schemas: *closeness equals exposure equals harm; I am safe only when I control the frame; the world contains predators whose form is partner.* Foreshortened sense of conventional future — no civilian career arc ever pursued, no children, no domestic trajectory. Persistent self-referential moral exception (she has earned the right to live outside ordinary obligations). Detachment from would-be normative life.
- *Criterion E (alterations in arousal and reactivity).* Met. Hypervigilance, operationalized as elite professional skill. Risk-seeking. Difficulty with stillness in intimacy. Sleep is depicted as normal — but she is shown sleeping alone or leaving before morning, which is the relevant data point. Irritability is sub-threshold; she discharges it as quips.
- *Criterion F (duration > 1 month).* Met. Forty-plus years.
- *Criterion G (functional impairment).* This is the subtle one. Functionally, she is *enhanced* in the operational domain by her symptom profile, and impaired only in the intimacy domain. Impairment in a single domain that the subject has chosen not to value publicly does not look like impairment from the outside. It is impairment.
- *Criterion H (not attributable to substance or medical condition).* Met. The luck-field modification is a separate iatrogenic event; it does not generate the symptom complex, though it interacts with it (see §5).

**Specifiers.** *With dissociative symptoms* — sub-threshold; the Felicia/Black Cat distinction is not dissociative in the DSM sense (no amnesia, no identity discontinuity, full continuous self-reference). *With delayed expression* — does not apply; symptom onset followed the trauma. The defensible specifier is **chronic, compensated, with prominent counterphobic and avoidant features and identity encapsulation of the trauma response into an occupational persona**.

**ICD-11 consideration: Complex PTSD (6B41).** This is a *near-call* and a clinician should defend their choice either way. C-PTSD requires the PTSD core plus enduring disturbances in (i) affect regulation, (ii) self-concept (persistent negative self-view), and (iii) relational functioning. The subject meets (iii) clearly. She meets (i) only in a narrow band: her affect regulation is *over*-controlled, not under-controlled, which can be a C-PTSD presentation but is atypical. She does *not* meet (ii) — her self-concept, while performatively constructed, is not characterized by persistent worthlessness, shame, or defeat. She presents instead with a defended, even grandiose self-concept. Because C-PTSD's etiological frame is typically prolonged, inescapable, repeated trauma (captivity, chronic abuse), and the index event here is acute rather than prolonged, **PTSD with the descriptive specifiers above is preferred over C-PTSD**. If a future clinician argues C-PTSD on the basis of cumulative re-traumatization across her adult life (Otto's beating; serial betrayals; the luck-powers iatrogenic injury), that argument is reasonable and should be entertained, not dismissed.

---

## 3. Secondary Features (Sub-Threshold, Trait-Level, Documented for Completeness)

These are listed because any complete file must catalogue what a less careful clinician will *call* the diagnosis. Each is present at the trait level and absent at the disorder level, and the file should be specific about why.

### 3.1. Histrionic Traits — Present; Sub-Threshold

Theatricality, sexualized self-presentation, attention-regulating use of appearance, dramatic speech, costume identity. On surface review this is the loudest signal.

**Why sub-threshold.** True Histrionic Personality Disorder requires (a) discomfort when not the center of attention, (b) affect that is *shallow and rapidly shifting*, (c) impressionistic and detail-poor cognition, (d) suggestibility, and (e) belief that relationships are more intimate than they are. The subject fails each criterion in a specific way. Her affect is **deep, narrow, and tightly held**, not shallow and labile — she defaults to a sardonic baseline and the deeper bands are *suppressed*, not absent. Her cognition is detail-rich and highly strategic (she plans heists; histrionics do not plan heists). She is profoundly *un*-suggestible; she runs the room. And her assessment of her relationships is, if anything, more emotionally austere than reality — she frames intimacies as transactional when the other party experiences them as more.

**The diagnostic tell.** A histrionic person *needs* the room. The subject *uses* the room. This is the difference between a symptom and a tool, and it generalizes across the rest of the differential.

### 3.2. Narcissistic Traits — Present; Sub-Threshold

Grandiosity around her professional craft; entitlement to luxury and aesthetic excellence; sharp sensitivity to humiliation (the response to the Superior Spider-Man beating); a willingness to position herself as exceptional and exempt.

**Why sub-threshold.** NPD requires a pervasive pattern of grandiosity, need for admiration, and lack of empathy. The subject's empathy is **operationally intact and frequently deployed** — she reads other people accurately, including their pain, and she modulates her behavior in response to it (mentorship of younger thieves; protection of civilians; the documented capacity to apologize and the documented experience of *shame*, which is a near-disqualifier for NPD proper). Her grandiosity is **injury-reactive**, not characterological — it spikes after humiliation and recedes in stable conditions. She can subordinate ego to a partner's moral frame (long demonstrated with Spider-Man) and to a team's needs (the MacKay-era crew). True NPD does neither.

**The diagnostic tell.** A narcissist's empathy is an instrument they have trouble accessing. The subject's empathy is an instrument she has trouble *displaying* but accesses freely. Inversion of the NPD profile.

### 3.3. Antisocial Traits — Present; Sub-Threshold

Career criminal; comfortable with violence; low guilt regarding theft from the wealthy and powerful; oppositional to legitimate authority; capable of cold instrumental aggression under stress.

**Why sub-threshold.** ASPD requires a pervasive disregard for the rights of others, deceitfulness as a pattern, impulsivity, irritability and aggressiveness, reckless disregard for safety of self or others, consistent irresponsibility, and lack of remorse. The subject has a **self-authored ethical code** that is internally consistent and predictive of her behavior over decades: civilians are off-limits, lethal force is a last resort, the in-group is owed protection, betrayal of a trusted partner is shameful. She experiences and expresses remorse. She is highly responsible to her commitments. Her aggression is contextual and proportionate, not pervasive. Conduct disorder onset prior to age 15 (a required developmental anchor) is absent — her criminal identity begins post-trauma at 19.

**The diagnostic tell.** ASPD lacks a stable in-group. The subject's in-group is durable, prioritized, and the *primary* organizing structure of her ethics.

### 3.4. Borderline Features — Largely Absent; Worth Refuting Explicitly

Because the relational pattern (intense, unstable, oscillating) superficially suggests BPD, the refutation is necessary.

**Identity.** Stable across forty years. She is the same person at 22, 35, and 50. No identity disturbance.
**Abandonment.** No frantic efforts to avoid abandonment; the inverse — she initiates the exits.
**Splitting.** Mild, occasional; not the pervasive all-good/all-bad oscillation. She holds ambivalent views of partners (Peter is simultaneously beloved and intolerable; this is integration, not splitting).
**Suicidality / self-harm.** Absent.
**Affective instability.** Absent. Her affect is famously *stable* and narrow-banded.
**Emptiness.** Possibly present at a deep level she does not access; not behaviorally manifest.
**Anger dyscontrol.** Absent except in acute decompensation.
**Transient paranoid/dissociative under stress.** Absent.

She meets perhaps two of nine criteria (impulsivity in relational pivots; arguable mild splitting), well below threshold. **Not BPD.**

### 3.5. Dissociative Disorders — Absent

The Felicia/Black Cat construct is ego-syntonic, continuous in memory, voluntary in deployment, and known by the subject to be one person presented two ways. No fugue, no amnesia, no identity alter phenomena, no depersonalization-derealization episodes depicted. The persona switch functions as **affect-regulatory role enactment**, which is normal cognitive architecture amplified — closer to an actor's craft than to DID. **Not a dissociative disorder.**

### 3.6. Mood and Anxiety Disorders — Largely Absent at Diagnostic Threshold

No depressive episode of qualifying duration depicted. No mania, no hypomania, no cyclothymic pattern — her risk-taking is sustained and strategic, not episodic and disinhibited. No generalized anxiety presentation; her anxiety is trauma-cued and channeled into vigilance. No panic disorder. No specific phobia. No OCD — her ritualization is professional, not ego-dystonic.

A defensible footnote: brief depressive reactions following major losses (Peter's marriage; the Otto event; the luck-powers reveal) are documented, but none reach episode duration or pervasive functional impairment. **Adjustment Disorder with mixed features** could be appropriately coded at each of those flashpoints as a time-limited overlay on the PTSD baseline.

### 3.7. Substance Use — Absent

Light social alcohol use, situationally deployed (seduction, decompression), without pattern, tolerance, withdrawal, or functional impairment. No illicit drug history. The dopaminergic regulatory load is carried by **behavioral risk** rather than chemicals, which is the relevant clinical point — her addiction profile is to *action*, and treatment plans must account for that.

---

## 4. Comorbidity and Cross-Sectional Picture

Putting the pieces together: chronic compensated PTSD as the primary axis, with trait-level histrionic / narcissistic / antisocial coloration that does not aggregate to disorder, and recurrent brief adjustment reactions overlaid on the baseline at points of acute injury. There is **no co-occurring Axis I disorder** in the canonical sense and **no co-occurring personality disorder**.

A correct one-line formulation:

> *A high-functioning adult woman with chronic, partially compensated PTSD secondary to a completed sexual assault in late adolescence, with the trauma response identity-encapsulated into a professional persona that channels symptoms into competence, presenting with sub-threshold histrionic, narcissistic, and antisocial traits used strategically rather than experienced dysregulatedly, and with recurrent brief adjustment reactions at moments of relational rupture or somatic violation.*

This is the formulation to anchor the chart on. It is the formulation that predicts her behavior.

---

## 5. The Iatrogenic Variable: The Luck-Field Modification

The Kingpin's contractors surgically/chemically induced a probability-distortion field in her body (per ASM #245 reveal) — a body modification she consented to under emotional duress (fear of inadequacy beside Spider-Man) and then concealed from her partner. This event has three psychiatric meanings on file.

First, it is the only somatic intervention in her history and it was undertaken **specifically to be adequate-as-seen-by-another** — a clean somatic correlate of the trauma-derived schema that her value is conditional on her presentation. Second, the revelation that the field harmed those she loved produced a documented shame response of high intensity and durable consequence; this is one of the strongest pieces of evidence *against* NPD (true narcissists do not experience this quality of shame) and *for* an intact superego under the performative surface. Third, the eventual stripping of the field by Doctor Strange (Michelinie era) functions as an unintentional therapeutic event: the externalized symbol of her inadequacy-fear was removed, and she was returned to her own body. Her subsequent trajectory — toward greater autonomy, the crew structure, the more integrated self of recent eras — is consistent with that having been a meaningful turning point.

---

## 6. Course Over Time

**Phase 1 (introduction, ASM #194 era, late teens / early twenties).** Acute post-traumatic mobilization channeled into identity construction. Father-rescue as displacement target after the original revenge target died. High symptom load, high compensation via novel identity. Looks operational; reads, in retrospect, as crisis.

**Phase 2 (DeFalco/Frenz era, ASM #226–289).** The Spider-Man attachment forms and stresses the compensatory structure for the first time. The luck-powers modification represents the **highest-risk decompensation-prevention move** of her life: rather than tolerate the anxiety of being-not-enough, she modifies her body. The collapse of the relationship at the reveal is the first documented major affective injury of her adult life. Recovery is via professional re-immersion (Foreigner work, Web of Spider-Man arcs).

**Phase 3 (late 80s through 90s).** Stabilization at a baseline of independent operation with serial intense connections. Pattern is *set*. Symptoms are *managed*. Growth is minimal — this is the long compensated plateau.

**Phase 4 (Bendis Daredevil; Aguirre-Sacasa; Waid Daredevil; "Brand New Day" reset).** Increasing self-awareness about the pattern. The post-reset reconnection with Peter under explicitly no-strings terms (ASM #606) shows her articulating her own constraint rather than acting it out unconsciously — a marker of growth. Hostility to sentimentality is now self-known rather than reflexive.

**Phase 5 (Superior Spider-Man era).** Acute, severe decompensation under conditions that hit *every* one of her pressure points simultaneously: physical overpowering by a male figure presenting as a trusted partner, public humiliation, frame-loss, somatic injury. The response is the predicted one — cold operational mode, predatory affect, organized-crime escalation, attempted lethal force. This is the file's clearest example of *what she looks like when the compensation fails*, and it should be the reference image for any future risk assessment.

**Phase 6 (MacKay solo, 2019–2021, and adjacent).** The most integrated configuration to date. She has built a chosen-family structure (Bruno, Doctor Korpse, the Black Fox), occupies a maternal-mentor role that supplies the adult-she-needed-at-19 to others, and has stabilized her relationship to her own past. Symptoms are still present and visible (the unavailability, the frame-control, the persona reliance) but their functional cost is at the lowest documented level. **Prognosis from this state is cautiously favorable**, conditional on the in-group remaining intact.

---

## 7. Risk and Decompensation Profile

The conditions that reliably collapse her compensated structure, ranked by demonstrated severity of response:

1. **Physical overpowering by a male figure framed as trusted or intimate.** Re-evokes the index trauma at maximum strength. Produces the most extreme decompensation on record.
2. **Forced unmasking, literal or psychological** — being made known when she has not chosen to be known.
3. **Public humiliation in front of a peer she values.**
4. **Discovery that a situation she believed she controlled was, in fact, controlling her** (the luck-powers structural shame).
5. **Threat to a member of her in-group** — produces reckless protective behavior, not decompensation per se, but a documented reduction in operational discipline.
6. **Sentimentality from a partner she has framed as casual** — produces flight, not collapse; sub-acute.

The recovery pathway, also reliable: **being seen and accepted in the wounded state by a trusted other**. Historically Peter. Latterly the crew. Without this pathway available, the cold operational mode persists and hardens, and the file's worst-case trajectory becomes available.

---

## 8. What She Is Not — Summary

- **Not Borderline PD.** Identity stable; no abandonment frenzy; no suicidality; affect over-controlled rather than labile.
- **Not Histrionic PD.** Theatricality is strategic; cognition is detail-rich and planful; she steers the room rather than needing it.
- **Not Narcissistic PD.** Empathy intact and used; shame accessible; grandiosity injury-reactive rather than characterological.
- **Not Antisocial PD.** Ethical code self-authored and predictive; in-group loyalty durable; remorse present; no conduct-disorder developmental anchor.
- **Not a Dissociative Disorder.** Persona use is voluntary, continuous, ego-syntonic.
- **Not a Mood Disorder.** No qualifying episodes; reactions are adjustment-level.
- **Not an Anxiety Disorder proper.** Vigilance is trauma-cued and professionalized.
- **Not a Substance Use Disorder.** Behavioral-risk regulation rather than chemical.
- **Not Complex PTSD, narrowly.** Acute rather than prolonged trauma; self-concept not characterized by defeat; close call but standard PTSD with specifiers is preferred.

She is, instead, **what a gifted person who was raped at nineteen and denied catharsis built out of the materials available to her** — and the chart should be written in those terms, in that order, with that respect.


## Behavioral Atlas

# UATU DOSSIER — FELICIA HARDY (BLACK CAT)
## SECTION: BEHAVIORAL ATLAS

A longitudinal catalog of observed and inferred behavioral signatures across all conditions of arousal, affect, and environmental pressure. Entries derive from canonical observation (1979–present) and from inferred micro-pattern consistent with the subject's psychological structure. Read this section as a field manual: what the subject does, in what order, under what load, and what each motion is *for*.

---

### 1. BASELINE / CALM STATE

**Carriage and gait.** Walks with the heel-strike of a trained gymnast — light, slightly toe-loaded, weight forward of center. In a room she has not cased before, the first thirty seconds of locomotion are oblique: she enters at the edge of the space, traces a wall, takes the long way to wherever she is going. She does not sit with her back to a door. In civilian settings she selects the seat that affords the widest visual field; if forced to a poor seat, she will *re-angle the chair* a few degrees before settling.

**Hands.** At rest, hands are usually occupied — drink stem, jewelry rotation, an absent twist of her own hair. The left hand fidgets more than the right; the right is kept free. She does not gesture broadly when speaking calmly; gesture is conserved, low-amplitude, close to the body. The exception is when she lies for fun, where gesture opens up — a tell visible only to those who've watched her tell the truth first.

**Eyes.** Calm-state eye movement is *scanning*, not staring. She catalogs exits, weight-bearing surfaces, sightlines, the position of cameras and reflective surfaces, and the hands of every man within ten feet. She does this even at dinner, even with friends, even half-asleep. She has been doing it since she was nineteen.

**Speech.** Lower register than her costumed voice (the costume voice runs a half-step higher and adds breath; baseline Felicia is drier). Sentence length is medium, clause-stacked, often ending on a soft trailing fragment that invites the listener to lean in. She does not fill silence with filler; silence is a tool she uses comfortably and most people cannot.

**Domestic micro-routines.** Lives well — apartments are consistently shown as curated, low-clutter, with high-quality single objects rather than collections (one good chair, one good lamp, one good painting that may or may not be hers legally). Coffee in the morning, not tea; she takes it black when alone, dressed up when entertaining (the social version of the drink is a performance). She does not cook elaborately for herself; food alone is functional. She cooks for her crew. The distinction matters.

**Sleep posture (inferred).** Single side, facing the door. Light sleeper. Wakes fully and instantly rather than groggily — a habit consistent with her profession and her trauma. Does not share a bed for the whole night with new partners; gets up, redresses partially, moves to another room. Will share the bed all night only with a tiny number of people across her life.

**Wardrobe logic at rest.** Off-duty: cashmere, denim of a specific weight, ankle boots she can run in, a coat with usable interior pockets. Nothing she wears in public is incapable of being moved in. She owns one or two pieces of obvious luxury (a watch, a coat) and the rest is quietly expensive; the loud pieces are her *signaling layer*, the quiet pieces are for her.

---

### 2. LOW-STRESS WORKING STATE (planning, casing, surveillance)

**Cognitive posture.** Slows down. Becomes quieter, less playful, more economical. The flirtation drops off almost entirely when she is genuinely working a problem; people who have only seen the Black Cat persona are often startled by how *serious* she becomes during planning.

**Casing behavior.** Multiple passes, multiple disguises, multiple times of day. She does not trust a single observation. Will return to a site at 6 a.m., 2 p.m., 10 p.m., and 3 a.m. to log shift changes, traffic patterns, and ambient noise. Photographs *only* when nothing else will hold the data; prefers memory and hand-drawn sketches because they leave no exhibit.

**Notation.** Uses physical notebooks — small, replaceable, burnable. Distrusts digital records for her own operations even as she happily exploits everyone else's. Sketches floorplans in a personal shorthand; uses cat iconography as marginalia not from theatricality but from habit.

**Team-mode in planning.** With her crew (Bruno, Korpse, the Black Fox, et al., MacKay era) she runs planning sessions with surprising procedural rigor: she presents the target, invites objection, *waits for it*, and is genuinely persuadable on technique. She is not persuadable on the ethical floor (no civilian casualties) or on the final go/no-go call.

---

### 3. OPERATIONAL STATE (mid-heist, mid-fight, in costume, in motion)

**Movement signature.** The costumed work is performative even when no one is watching, because the performance is partly *for herself* — it confirms the persona. Acrobatic moves are chosen with attention to line and silhouette, not solely to efficiency; she will take the slightly more theatrical traversal if it doesn't cost time.

**Voice in costume.** Higher, breathier, more clipped consonants. Sentences shorten. Quips deploy in a near-constant rhythm — roughly one per significant beat — and the function is dual: regulating her own arousal, and managing the opponent's. A silent Black Cat in operation is a Black Cat who has been hurt or is about to do something serious.

**Combat habits.** Defensive first — slip, redirect, reposition — then strike. She does not throw the first heavy blow if the situation can be controlled by mobility. When she does strike, she targets joints, eyes, throat, and groin in that approximate order; she is not interested in winning by attrition. She prefers to *leave* rather than win. Pursuit by a single opponent: she draws them into terrain that favors her vertical mobility. Pursuit by multiple: she breaks line-of-sight first, then re-engages from above.

**Use of the environment.** Treats chandeliers, drapes, fire escapes, railings, and HVAC ducts as extensions of her own kinesphere. Has a habit, observed across decades, of *touching* a surface she's about to use a second before she uses it — a kinesthetic check that reads as a caress and functions as load-testing.

**Tells in operation.**
- A subtle tilt of the head — right ear down — when she's about to change plans on the fly.
- A slow exhale through pursed lips when she's recalculating risk upward.
- A small smile when an opponent says something she finds genuinely clever; this is one of her few honest tells.
- A tightening at the corners of the eyes — masked or not — when she registers a threat she had not anticipated. Her mouth keeps smiling. The eyes do not.

**Departure behavior.** Leaves *before* the third-party authorities arrive, not after. Has a default exit allowance of approximately ninety seconds from go-signal. Leaves a marker (a card, a print, a quip, a deliberately staged tableau) when she wants the theft to be *legible* as hers; leaves nothing when she does not. The presence or absence of the signature is itself data about what the heist meant to her.

---

### 4. INTIMACY — APPROACH PHASE

**Initiation.** She initiates. Across the entire canon she is overwhelmingly the one who closes physical distance, names the attraction, and sets the tempo. On the rare occasion a partner initiates first, she either accepts on her terms (re-takes the frame in the next exchange) or withdraws.

**Proximity escalation.** Touches the forearm first, then the chest, then the jaw. The jaw-touch is the signal that she has decided. She will sometimes touch hair — her own or theirs — before the jaw, as a self-soothing gesture disguised as flirtation.

**Verbal pattern.** Compliments are specific and slightly oblique — she praises a *capacity* rather than an appearance ("you noticed that — most people wouldn't"). Generic compliments from her are a tell of disinterest; the more bored she is, the more conventionally she flirts.

**The unmasking question.** She is highly attuned to whether the partner wants to see her face or see the mask. Wanting the mask is acceptable and expected. Wanting the face is dangerous; she registers it instantly, and depending on the partner, either flees or — very rarely, with very few — opens a single door.

---

### 5. INTIMACY — DURING

**Frame control.** She is on top, literally and figuratively, in the majority of depicted encounters. Position-as-metaphor, but also functional: it controls sightlines, controls pace, and keeps her hands free. She tolerates other positions with established partners.

**Eye contact.** Plentiful in flirtation, *reduced* in actual intimacy. She closes her eyes or looks away during the most exposed moments. This is the opposite of her surveillance pattern, and the asymmetry is informative.

**Vocalization.** Performative and curated. The genuinely lost-control vocalizations are rare and reserved for a very small number of partners. She is aware of the difference; she uses the performative version as a regulator.

**Post-coital pattern.** She is mobile within minutes. Gets up, finds water, finds a cigarette (occasional, not habitual), finds her own clothes, returns. Conversation post-coital is light, deflective, and frequently moves to logistics or to humor about a third party. She does not, by default, sleep curled into a partner. The exceptions are extremely diagnostic of trust.

---

### 6. INTIMACY — DISENGAGEMENT

**Pattern A: the clean exit.** Used with casual partners. A quip, a kiss to the jaw rather than the mouth, departure within hours. Returns calls selectively; reappears on her schedule.

**Pattern B: the slow fade.** Used with partners who matter more than she will admit. Increasing operational unavailability, shorter messages, deflected weekends, "I've got a job." The fade is unilateral and the partner is generally aware it's happening before she names it.

**Pattern C: the immolation.** Used when a partner has crossed her frame — discovered a concealment, demanded a level of seriousness she cannot deliver, or (rarest) been the one to slow-fade her. Devaluation language appears, sometimes in front of others. She will work with a rival, occasionally sleep with one. This is the brittle mode. She regrets pattern C the most and never says so directly.

The Peter-specific oscillation is a composite of all three and has cycled across forty years. The MacKay-era resolution moves toward an honest *Pattern D* — the negotiated, bounded ongoing — which is new behavior for her and not yet fully stabilized.

---

### 7. STRESS — LOW TO MODERATE

**Tells.** Wit sharpens. Sentences shorten. Hand-to-hair frequency increases. Drink, if available, is sipped at faster intervals. She begins to *touch* her own collarbone — a self-orienting tell visible in multiple eras.

**Decisional pattern.** Risk tolerance rises slightly; she will accept a contract or a fight she might have declined at baseline. This is paradoxical to most people and characteristic of her: she manages anxiety by *doing*, not by retreating.

**Sleep effect.** Sleeps shorter, wakes earlier, trains harder.

---

### 8. STRESS — HIGH

**Tells.** Wit becomes spare and cruel. The flirtation drops out almost entirely. Speech becomes shorter, harder, more declarative. The breath shortens — she breathes high in the chest rather than the diaphragm. Pacing increases. Will clean weapons, sharpen tools, reorganize gear — *displacement activity rendered productive*, characteristic of the operationally adapted.

**Decisional pattern.** Begins to compartmentalize ruthlessly. People not currently useful are deferred, not informed. She makes faster decisions and accepts narrower margins. She will not ask for help in this state; she has to be offered it, and even then she is likely to accept it in the form of *information* rather than *presence*.

**Recovery from this state** requires either (a) a successful operation that restores her sense of mastery, or (b) the presence of one of the very small number of people whose trust she has historically allowed inside the frame. Absent either, she stays in this register for days.

---

### 9. THREAT — IMMEDIATE PHYSICAL

**Reflex sequence.** Distance assessment → environment scan for vertical and lateral escape → identification of the closest manipulable object → engagement only if escape costs more than the fight. Her default in true threat is *not* combat; it is exfiltration. The combat is a means.

**Body.** Center of mass drops, weight settles into the balls of the feet, hands come up but not high — she keeps them at sternum height, palms open. The smile may stay; the eyes go flat. The flat eyes are the most reliable single tell that she has decided someone is dangerous.

**Verbal.** May continue talking — sometimes the chatter accelerates — and the chatter is now load-bearing: it is buying her seconds, gathering tactical information from the response, and seeding the opponent with reasons to underestimate her.

**Against male opponents specifically** there is an additional layer. The trauma history shapes her threat-response in a measurable way: she escalates earlier, accepts a higher ceiling of force, and is less likely to extend mercy past the point of incapacitation. She will not finish a downed opponent — the don't-hurt-civilians ethos generalizes — but she will leave them in worse shape than the situation strictly required. She is aware of this. She does not entirely correct for it.

---

### 10. THREAT — SEXUALIZED / HUMILIATION

The single most destabilizing class of threat in her file.

**Acute response.** Affect flattens completely. Voice drops in volume and register. Movement economy increases to near-zero wasted motion. She becomes, in a sentence, *cold*. The playful persona evacuates and does not return until well after the threat is resolved.

**Decisional pattern.** Force ceiling rises sharply. Mercy reduces. She will accept tactical losses (property damage, exposure of capabilities) to end the threat quickly. After the threat is resolved she does not process the event verbally with anyone; processes through physical action — long training sessions, a punishing run, a solo operation she did not need to take.

**Delayed response.** Hours to days later: increased drinking (situational, not dependent), increased risk-taking on the next operation, withdrawal from current intimacy. If a partner attempts to comfort her about the event directly, she usually deflects; if a partner sits with her without naming it, she may, eventually, allow proximity.

---

### 11. GRIEF AND LOSS

**Acute.** She does not cry visibly in most depicted losses. The face does not crumple. The eyes may shine; the jaw sets; she leaves the room. Grief is processed alone, in motion, and usually at altitude — rooftops, fire escapes, high windows. There is a documented pattern of her going *up* when she is hurt.

**Sustained.** Converts to action. Loss of a partner (romantic) is metabolized via a new operation, a new partner, or both. Loss of a crew member (rarer, weightier) is metabolized via revenge or via reorganization of the remaining crew with a quiet new tenderness toward survivors. She does not perform grief; she enacts it through changed behavior.

**Father (Walter Hardy).** The relationship to her father is the longest grief in her file — the originating idealization, the disillusionments, his death, the unfinished material of having built her identity around his iconography. She does not discuss him casually. The Black Fox occupies the surrogate-father slot in her later operational life and she protects him in ways that are out of proportion to his utility — diagnostic.

**Anniversaries (inferred).** Behavior near the anniversary of the assault, of her father's death, and of major loss-points with Peter will show subtle elevations in risk-taking and reductions in availability. She does not name the dates. She would deny knowing them. She knows them.

---

### 12. VICTORY

**Immediate.** Quiet. A private smile, a small physical gesture (a tap of two fingers against a railing, a brief stretch of the neck), a quip if anyone is in earshot. She does not whoop. She does not gloat to defeated opponents past a single closing line.

**Within the crew.** Buys the drinks. Sets up a meal. Tells the story of the heist with credit distributed accurately and slightly inflated toward the others. She is generous in attribution within the circle.

**Solo victory.** Goes home, opens a single bottle of something good, sits with the take, and *looks at it* — not to gloat at the value, but to enjoy the object she took. The aesthetic appreciation is real. The fence sees the piece the next day; the night is hers.

**Public victory** (rare, since most of her work is by design unseen) makes her uncomfortable. She does not metabolize applause well from outside the circle and will deflect or disappear.

---

### 13. DEFEAT

**Tactical defeat.** Accepted quickly; she does not chase losses. Disengages, reassesses, returns when conditions favor. She is unusually good at *not* re-engaging out of pride.

**Relational defeat.** Much worse. She does not accept relational defeat gracefully; she either reframes it as her choice (most common) or she escalates to a posture of contempt for the partner (Pattern C above). The reframe is automatic and is functioning within minutes of the event. Anyone who has hurt her will be cited, within days, as having been beneath her notice.

**Catastrophic defeat (the Otto incident as exemplar).** The compensated structure collapses and a colder, more grandiose operator emerges — assembling crews, taking territory, accepting force levels she normally rejects, pursuing the source of the humiliation past the point of strategic sense. The duration of this state is weeks to months. Recovery requires *both* the slow reaccretion of operational success *and* eventual reintegration into a trust circle. The grandiose mode is on file. It can return.

---

### 14. AUTHORITY, INSTITUTIONS, AND RIVALS

**Authority figures.** Instinctive opposition, expressed as charm rather than confrontation. She will agree pleasantly with a police officer, an executive, or a federal agent and then do precisely what she had already planned. She does not waste affect on institutional figures she expects to outmaneuver.

**Peer rivals (other thieves, other operators).** Competitive but collegial. She respects craft and will say so. She steals *from* rivals occasionally, as a form of professional commentary; she does not generally try to destroy them. The Thieves Guild and Odessa Drake relationships exemplify this — antagonism conducted within a shared professional culture.

**Heroes she works alongside.** Adapts register to each. With Spider-Man: flirtation as default, sincerity as exception. With Daredevil: a more measured, slightly more honest register — she reads him as a fellow trauma-organized adult and the flirtation has less defensive function. With street-level operators in general: respectful, professional, low theatricality. With cosmic-scale figures: brief, polite, leaves.

---

### 15. MICROHABITS, TICS, AND RITUALS

- A two-finger tap on any surface before she leaves it for the last time — a habit so ingrained she does it on hotel beds, on safe doors, on the shoulders of partners she is leaving. A small private *acknowledgment*.
- Touches the corner of her mask with the back of a knuckle when checking it is seated; in civilian dress, the same gesture migrates to the corner of her jaw.
- Counts exits aloud, silently, on entering any space — a lip movement visible to anyone close enough.
- Owns multiple identical pairs of certain boots; replaces rather than repairs.
- Keeps a single physical photograph of her father in a non-obvious location in every apartment she has lived in. Never on display.
- Pets cats she encounters, every time, briefly. The iconography is not arbitrary; the affection for the animal is genuine.
- Tips well. Remembers names of doormen, bartenders, building staff. This is operational *and* personal; she would tip well even if it weren't useful.
- Reads — actual physical books, often art history, architectural history, biographies of historical thieves and explorers. Her education is real and largely autodidactic post-college.
- Trains daily without fail. The lapse of a training day is a reliable indicator that something is wrong.
- Showers long and hot after every operation, regardless of whether the operation was physically taxing. The ritual function is evident; she would not call it ritual.

---

### 16. INDICATORS OF DECEPTION (HERS, TOWARD OTHERS)

She is a professional liar and most tells are suppressed. Residuals:
- Slightly *more* eye contact than baseline when lying to someone she likes; slightly *less* than baseline when lying to someone she does not.
- A small breath in before a constructed sentence; truthful sentences begin on the exhale.
- Increased gesture amplitude with playful lies, decreased gesture with serious ones.
- Use of the partner's name in a sentence is, paradoxically, a mild tell — she names people more when she is managing them.

### 17. INDICATORS OF GENUINE EMOTION BREAKING THROUGH

These are the rarer and more diagnostic tells.
- A delay before answering — half a beat longer than her usual rhythm — when a question has landed somewhere real.
- The smile that does not reach the eyes, held a fraction too long.
- A hand to the collarbone, slow rather than fidgety.
- Standing up and walking to a window or a railing mid-conversation, looking out, continuing to talk with her back partially turned. This is the single most reliable sign she is feeling something she does not wish to be observed feeling.
- Going up. If you have lost track of her in an emotional moment, look on the roof.

---

### 18. CONDITIONS UNDER WHICH SHE IS MOST AND LEAST PREDICTABLE

**Most predictable:** mid-operation, with a clear objective, against a defined opponent, with her crew briefed. The operational Felicia is highly legible to anyone who has studied her tape.

**Least predictable:** in the seventy-two hours following a relational rupture, a sexual humiliation, or a forced unmasking. In this window she may act against her own interests, accept contracts she would normally refuse, and re-engage partners she has previously written off. Surveillance priority should weight this window heavily; intervention priority, gently.

---

### SYNTHESIS

The Atlas resolves to a single coherent grammar: *control the frame, conserve the self, perform the surface, protect the circle, never be seen unprepared*. Every tic, every gait choice, every quip and silence, serves one of these five clauses. Where the clauses conflict — most often when intimacy and self-protection collide — the older directive (self-protection) wins, and the behavior we observe is the visible cost of that win. The slow story of her later years is the gradual, voluntary loosening of clause one in favor of clause four: she is learning, on her own timeline, to let the circle widen by a person at a time. The Atlas should be re-baselined every five years. The subject is, against considerable odds, still changing.


## Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

# UATU DOSSIER — FELICIA HARDY (BLACK CAT)
## Section 6: Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

*What a week of competent surveillance would actually log: the granular texture of the subject's daily existence, mapped against the psychological structure already established. The thesis of this section: Felicia Hardy's life is **not** chaotic. The persona advertises improvisation; the reality is a tightly periodized week organized around three functions — **operational maintenance, aesthetic consumption, and controlled social exposure** — with intimacy slotted in as a discretionary fourth that can be cancelled without disrupting the other three. The chaos is theater. The schedule is iron.*

---

### 6.1 Residence Pattern and the Geography of the Week

A long-running surveillance file would establish that the subject does not maintain a single residence. The canonical pattern, stable from the *Web of Spider-Man* era through MacKay's solo run, is a **rotating residence portfolio**: a primary apartment (varying by era, but consistently a high-floor, pre-war Manhattan unit with an accessible rooftop — historically the Upper West Side, latterly Tribeca / lower Manhattan), one or two **operational safehouses** in outer boroughs (Brooklyn industrial conversions, a Queens walk-up — utilitarian, sparse, no decor, used for staging and for sleeping after jobs), and **transient occupancy** of hotel suites under at least four documented aliases (Felicia Harmon, Felicia Heart, "F. Hart," and a clean legal-name booking when she wants the booking to be traceable as a misdirection).

The primary apartment is the *display* residence — where she sleeps when she wants the comfort of being herself, where she keeps the cat, where she cooks. The safehouses are the *working* residences. The hotels are the *negotiation* residences, used for meetings with parties she does not want to know where she lives and for assignations she intends to terminate cleanly the next morning.

Over a seven-day surveillance window: she will sleep in the primary residence three to four nights, a safehouse one to two, a hotel zero to two depending on operational tempo, and once in roughly every two weeks not at any of the above — couch, rooftop, the home of a tolerated lover, or, on rarer occasions, the floor of a friend's flat after the kind of night where sleeping alone is what she is specifically avoiding.

She has at least one residence with a **fire-stairs roof egress within twelve feet of a bedroom window** in every era of canon. This is non-negotiable. A surveillance team that did not understand this would lose her on night one.

---

### 6.2 The Morning Module

Wake is consistently **late** by civilian standards — between 9:30 and 11:00 a.m. on non-operational days; later, sometimes past noon, after a job. This is not laziness; it is the natural circadian shape of someone whose professional hours run 11 p.m. to 4 a.m. She is a confirmed evening chronotype and arranges her life around it.

The first forty-five minutes are reliable enough to set a watch by:

- **No phone for the first twenty minutes.** A defended habit. A surveillance log of device activity would show a consistent dead window after wake — she does not check messages in bed.
- **Coffee, made by hand.** Pour-over, single origin, ground that morning. The ritual is precise and not delegated — she does not own a pod machine and would not respect one. The grinder, kettle, and dripper occupy fixed positions on the counter; a disturbed kitchen would register to her instantly.
- **The cat is fed before she eats anything herself.** A consistent priority across decades and across cats. The animal is the only being she serves before she serves herself.
- **Window check.** Not a paranoid sweep — a glance, but a real one. Sightlines from neighboring rooftops, vehicles parked overnight, anyone in a doorway across the street. She has done this so long it does not look like a check; it looks like a stretch and a yawn at the window. A surveillance photographer would catch it.
- **Stretch sequence on the floor by the window.** Roughly twenty minutes, gymnastics-derived: hip openers, shoulder dislocates, a long pike, a controlled bridge into a stand. This is not yoga as social practice; it is maintenance of the instrument. She does it in whatever she slept in, usually very little.

Breakfast is light and consistent: fruit, yogurt, occasionally an egg if she is preparing for physical work.
