She does not depict a single named style because there is no single named style. The portfolio reads as a syllabus designed by someone who *researched what would have stopped what happened to her* and built outward from there. That is its own diagnostic.

**Weapons.**

- *Grapple line / bullwhip*. Her most frequent secondary tool. Used for swinging (with technical inferiority to webbing — shorter range, anchor-dependent, less reusable), pulling weapons from hands, ankle-snaring, descents from height. Stowed at hip, drawn by feel.
- *Sidearm-tier firearms* — present but rare. She owns and can shoot; she avoids it. The avoidance is *ethical-tactical*: noise, lethality, chain-of-custody. Operationally she treats guns as evidence she would rather not generate.
- *Improvised weapons.* High proficiency. Will use chandelier chain, broken champagne flute, gallery rope-stand, an opponent's own collapsed baton.
- *Specialty kit (MacKay-era).* Lockpicks, RF jammers, magnetic crampons, EMP grenades, smoke pellets — see §6.5.

**Combat philosophy.** Avoid engagement. If engaged, end inside three exchanges. If unable to end it, exit. Never fight on someone else's chosen ground if a choice exists. She does not enjoy combat the way several other costumed thieves in her ecosystem do — combat for Felicia is a *failure of plan*, and the speed with which she terminates fights reflects that. The exception is sparring/flirt-combat with Spider-Man, which she will extend deliberately because the engagement is the point.

---

### 6.4 The Probability Field ("Bad Luck Powers")

The most-discussed and most-misunderstood line item.

**Origin and mechanism.** Surgically and chemically induced by Kingpin's contractors in the early Owl/Octopus arcs, revealed in *ASM* #245 (O'Neil/Mooney). Mechanism is canonically vague but functionally consistent: in Felicia's proximity, low-probability negative events befall designated targets — equipment fails, footing gives, ricochets find improbable lines, ammunition jams. It is not telekinesis, not hex magic in the Scarlet Witch sense; it is a localized *bias* on stochastic outcomes.

**Range and parameters.**

- *Effective radius* — within visual range, attenuating with distance. Documented unreliable beyond approximately a city block.
- *Selectivity* — initially directable; she could choose a target by attention. This was the design spec.
- *Latency* — not instantaneous. Effects accumulate over seconds to minutes inside the field; sudden engagements get little benefit.
- *Conservation problem (the critical defect)* — the field, in operation, **leaks**. Bad luck experienced by the target is, in some accounts, balanced by an opposite or recursive load on those Felicia cares about. Peter is harmed repeatedly; this is the canonical betrayal of the gift.

**The Strange intervention.** Doctor Strange strips the field (Michelinie era, *ASM* circa #5 of vol. 2 by the Michelinie continuity). Replacement: Strange grants her a controllable *enhanced agility/balance* boost that is reliable and harmless. She uses this for some years; later writers quietly de-emphasize and then drop the residual, returning her to baseline peak-human (this is the current operating status, MacKay-era).

**Symptom-as-signature reading — the deepest tell in the entire file.** Felicia accepted a body-modification she did not need, in secret, from a man she despised, because she suspected her partner would consider her inadequate without it. The modification then *injured the partner*. The entire arc is the somatic literalization of her psychological architecture: alter the self to be adequate to the loved other; the alteration harms the loved other; the loved other discovers the alteration; intimacy collapses. The luck powers are not a power — they are a **diagnosis written in superhero idiom**. Their removal and her durable functioning without them is, correspondingly, a recovery marker.

---

### 6.5 Burglary as Discipline

This is her actual profession, and the file should treat it with the seriousness one would treat a surgeon's operative skill.

**Reconnaissance.** Pre-job intelligence cycles run weeks. Documented behaviors: physical site surveillance from multiple vantage points across multiple times of day; cover-identity penetration of staff layers (caterer, art handler, party guest); social engineering of low-level personnel for floorplan-adjacent detail; off-hours rooftop surveys of HVAC and electrical routing; review of building permit filings (publicly available, she uses them). She maintains a working mental model of the target before she ever enters.

**Defeat-the-system competencies.**

- *Mechanical locks* — picks any commercial pin-tumbler under thirty seconds; high-security (Medeco, Abloy) under two minutes; safe combinations by manipulation if the lock is older, by drilling-and-scoping if necessary, by social-engineering the combination from staff when available.
- *Electronic security* — defeats motion sensors via thermal-managed approach (slow, low body-presentation); bypasses pressure plates by weight-distribution and route; spoofs or loops camera feeds with portable kit (MacKay-era shows her crew, particularly Bruno, handling the back-end while she runs the floor).
- *Biometrics* — handled via social engineering, lifted prints, or crew-supplied prosthetics; she does not enjoy this layer and prefers jobs that don't require it.
- *Vault work* — competent but pragmatic; will defer to specialists in her crew when available.

**Movement inside a building.** Silent, three-dimensional, route-redundant (she always knows the second and third egress). Trained to read floor plans for negative space — service corridors, dumbwaiter shafts, between-floor utility access. Uses ceiling space and crawl voids that civilians forget exist.

**Exfiltration.** Her preferred exit is always *theatrical* and *unnecessary* — the rooftop leap, the wink at the camera on the way out, the calling card on the empty plinth. This is operationally suboptimal — clean exits are unmemorable exits — and she does it anyway, which is data. The signature is a confession of identity she will not otherwise make.

**Fence and disposition network.** Maintained relationships with the Black Fox, the Thieves Guild (variable), Odessa Drake's Manhattan operation (MacKay), occasional private collectors. She does not sit on inventory; turnover is fast.

---

### 6.6 Cognitive and Social Skills

**Pattern recognition and operational planning.** Genuinely gifted. She plans heists at a level that would credit a senior special-operations officer. She maintains contingency trees several deep, pre-positions resources, and runs operational deceptions (false jobs to misdirect security postings, decoy thieves). Across canon she is rarely beaten by counter-planning; she is beaten, when beaten, by being engaged unexpectedly by someone whose intervention she did not model — usually Spider-Man.

**Languages.** Functional French and Italian (depicted across European-set arcs); workable Spanish; some Japanese (MacKay-era museum job). She is not a polyglot in the Black Widow sense but she is comfortable on three continents.

**Social engineering.** First-tier. She can read a room's status hierarchy in under a minute, identify the lonely security director at the gala, calibrate flirtation to extract the specific piece of information she needs, and leave the mark *pleased to have met her*. The skill is built on close observation (micro-expression, posture, alcohol level, ring finger) and on willingness to deploy her own appearance instrumentally.

**Acting / cover identity.** Maintains multiple civilian-passing identities with documentation. Switches accent and physical register with a costume change. The persona work is fluent because the persona work is also her psychological default — the gap between "Felicia in cover" and "Felicia on a date" is smaller than she advertises.

**Limitations.** Cryptography, advanced electronics, network intrusion — she outsources. Forensic accounting and laundering — outsourced. Long-form deep-cover (months as a single identity) — has done it but dislikes it; her affect is too distinctive to fully suppress for extended periods.

---

### 6.7 Equipment

**Suit.** Black, form-fitting, fur trim at collar and cuffs (variable across eras), reinforced at vital lines. Recent depictions (MacKay) show clear armor weave at sternum and kidney, articulated knee/elbow plating cosmetically hidden, integrated grapple anchor at the belt. The suit is *engineered theater* — designed to draw and hold attention while concealing the protection that lets her survive drawing it.

**Mask and hair.** Domino mask preferred — preserves the lower face for kissing, smiling, and the deniable identity wedge (a domino does not conceal the way a full hood does, which means *being Black Cat* is a choice to be visible-as-Black-Cat rather than to disappear). The platinum hair is hers, untreated, distinctive — and operationally a liability she refuses to mitigate, because the hair is part of the signature.

**Claws.** Retractable, fingertip-mounted, edged for cutting line and clothing, capable of inflicting lacerating but typically non-lethal wounds. Useful for climbing rough vertical surfaces, scoring glass for silent cuts, and the occasional disarm.

**Grapnel / line.** Variable across eras; baseline a compact reel with a magnetic or grappling head, hundred-foot working line, rated to her body weight plus a hostage.

**Comms.** Standard professional-grade encrypted earpiece; crew net in MacKay era.

**Vehicles.** Motorcycle preferred (multiple depicted, generally fast Italian); competent driver of cars and helicopters; passable pilot for fixed-wing in emergencies.

**Safehouses.** Distributed across Manhattan — minimum three known to canon. Maintained with cash and care, never registered in her name, never used as residence.

---

### 6.8 Growth Across the Long Arc

Three distinct competence eras are visible in the file.

**Era 1 — Apprentice/Romantic (1979–1989, Wolfman through DeFalco).** Skills credible but inconsistently depicted; the luck powers do the heavy lifting in fights she should otherwise lose. Operational autonomy limited — she runs missions that orbit Spider-Man rather than independent jobs. Tactical signature: improvise, charm, escape.

**Era 2 — Journeyman/Independent (1990s–2000s, *Web of Spider-Man*, *Spider-Man Unlimited*, Bendis cameos, Smith retcon).** Powers stripped or de-emphasized; she compensates by deepening the burglary craft and the martial portfolio. The Foreigner association period gives her access to professional-mercenary tradecraft she retains permanently — counter-surveillance discipline, dead-drop protocols, weapons handling she previously waved off. Tactical signature: plan, execute, vanish.

**Era 3 — Master/Principal (2010s–present, MacKay's *Black Cat* solo, Wells's "Heist," ongoing).** Runs her own crew. Plans multi-stage operations across weeks. Mentors. Negotiates with the Thieves Guild, Odessa Drake, the Maggia. The luck powers are gone and unmissed; baseline craft is sufficient. Tactical signature: orchestrate, delegate, headline.

The arc is a real one: she has gotten *materially better* over forty years, not just narratively re-skinned. The trajectory is consistent with the psychological recovery curve — as the trauma compensates, the craft no longer needs the prosthesis.

---

### 6.9 Limits, Honestly Stated

- **Will lose to most metahuman bricks straight up.** She fights them by terrain, deception, or refusal.
- **Will lose to Spider-Man if he chooses to win.** Their parity in their scenes together is a courtesy he extends; she knows this; she has occasionally weaponized that knowledge.
- **Vulnerable to ranged fire she cannot read.** Sniper at distance, drone fire, area-effect weapons — she has no answer except cover and exit.
- **Vulnerable to opponents who do not respond to seduction or theater** — the Otto-as-Spider-Man encounter is the canonical case. Her tactical repertoire assumes a certain kind of social field; against opponents indifferent to that field she is reduced to her bare physical envelope, which is good but not invincible.
- **Vulnerable to forced unmasking** — psychologically destabilizing in a way that degrades tactical performance for hours to days following.
- **Limited offensive ceiling.** She is built to *take* — objects, opportunities, men's attention — not to *destroy*. When the situation calls for destruction she has to override her own grammar, which she can do, and which costs her.

---

### 6.10 The Through-Line

Every capability in this section was acquired or refined after a single nineteen-year-old night that her body could not stop. Read as a whole, the inventory is a forty-year project to make the body that failed her then *categorically incapable* of failing her again — and to ensure that any room she ever enters, she enters by her own choice and leaves by her own. The peak conditioning, the eclectic martial portfolio assembled from rape-defense outward, the surveillance-resistant tradecraft, the seduction calibrated as control rather than offer, the suit that is half armor and half advertisement, even the long-defunct probability field she let a man she hated install in her body to be adequate to a man she loved — each is the same sentence in a different grammar. *Never again on terms not mine.*

The powers, in the end, are the symptom rendered as competence. That she has built, out of that, a life with a crew, an ethic, a craft, and an aesthetic she actually loves — is the measure of the woman, not the measure of the wound.


## Operational Profile & Tradecraft

# UATU INTELLIGENCE DOSSIER — FELICIA HARDY (BLACK CAT)
## SECTION 6: OPERATIONAL PROFILE & TRADECRAFT

---

### 6.1 Decision Architecture

The subject's operational decision-making bifurcates cleanly along a line that is itself diagnostic: **target-selection is affect-driven; execution is coldly procedural.** Once a job is chosen — and the choosing is almost always emotionally over-determined (a piece that "should" belong to her, a mark who insulted a friend, a vault that has refused other thieves, a contract that will route her near a current romantic preoccupation) — the planning phase locks down into something close to engineering discipline.

Her standard cycle, observable across the Wolfman, DeFalco, MacKay, and Wells eras, runs roughly:

1. **Acquisition of interest** — usually triggered by rumor, gossip in fence circles, an art-world catalogue, an overheard remark at one of the high-end charity events she attends as Felicia Hardy, or a deliberately leaked target by a rival (the Foreigner, Odessa Drake, the Black Fox in mentor mode). She is unusually susceptible to *dare-shaped* intelligence; a job framed as impossible enters her queue automatically.
2. **Soft surveillance window, 5–14 days.** Felicia in civilian dress: gallery openings, fundraisers, hotel bars adjacent to the target. She gathers human intelligence first, architectural intelligence second. She talks to staff — concierges, security guards on smoke breaks, junior curators, the cleaning crew — and tips lavishly. She remembers names. She is gathering a *behavioral model of the building*, not a blueprint.
3. **Technical reconnaissance.** Blueprints (often pulled by Bruno Grainger from municipal/insurance databases), alarm specifications, guard rotations. Three independent walk-throughs minimum if the structure permits, at three different times of day.
4. **Rehearsal.** She physically rehearses ingress and egress in a comparable space when possible — gymnastic facilities, parking garages, her own loft mocked up. The rehearsal is *kinesthetic*; she does not trust a plan she has not put through her body.
5. **Execution with two pre-mapped abort points and a minimum of three egress routes.** She will walk away from a job she has spent three weeks on if the third egress is compromised. This is the discipline that has kept her uncaught across a forty-year operational career.
6. **Post-action cooling.** 48–72 hours minimum off the grid, no fence contact, no social presence. Then disposition of the take, then re-emergence.

The *flaw* in this architecture, predictable across decades, is that emotionally-loaded targets corrupt step 5. When Spider-Man is in the building, when Peter Parker is in the country, when a former lover is the mark — egress discipline degrades. She has been caught (and let herself be caught) more times than her skill level explains, and the variable is always relational.

---

### 6.2 Tradecraft — Physical Layer

**Movement.** Trained gymnast baseline overlaid with multiple striking arts (the *Evil That Men Do* training arc names judo and several others; her depicted technique blends judo throws, savate kicks, and a wrist-lock-heavy grappling style). She moves through buildings *vertically by default* — her instinct is up-and-over rather than through-and-out, a preference shaped by years of working alongside a wall-crawler and by gymnastics conditioning. Rooftops are her native terrain; she is observably less comfortable in basements, sewers, and confined horizontal infiltration, and avoids them when possible.

**Climbing rig.** Grappling line, retractable, mounted to a wrist gauntlet — the same basic system since the early Wolfman appearances, iteratively upgraded. Backup line on opposite forearm. She carries a secondary clip-and-rappel kit in the small-of-back compartment of the suit.

**The suit itself.** Functional combat/operational gear that has been allowed to read as fetish-coded for plausible-deniability reasons she fully understands and exploits: the visual register disarms male targets and male responders by 1–3 seconds, and she has built that interval into multiple escape calculations. The suit incorporates kevlar-weight reinforcement at the torso, climbing-friction pads at the inner thighs and palms, and a magnetic seam system she can shed in roughly four seconds to switch to a civilian outfit carried beneath or stashed at an egress point. The white wig/hair is a single-purpose disguise element — it changes her silhouette at distance and on camera, and she removes and discards it during civilian transitions.

**Weapons.** She does not carry firearms by preference and has been visibly contemptuous of crews that do. Standard kit: collapsible baton, several small smoke and flash devices, lockpicks (mechanical and electronic), a glass cutter, a thin diamond-tipped blade, occasional taser. Her hands and feet are the primary weapon system. Lethal force is available to her and she has used it under extremity, but the operational default is incapacitation.

**The luck field (historical).** During the period the bad-luck probability field was active, her tradecraft was *systematically corrupted* by it — she relied on it as a margin, and the file shows a measurable degradation of pure-skill technique during that window. Post-removal (Strange, Michelinie era) her skill-floor recovered and arguably exceeded the pre-augmentation baseline because she had to re-discipline. This is on file as a permanent lesson: she will not accept body-modification augmentation again without extreme cause.

---

### 6.3 Tradecraft — Information & Counter-Surveillance

She runs a **two-identity discipline** that is sloppy by professional intelligence standards but tight by costumed-criminal standards. Felicia Hardy is a known associate of Spider-Man and a sometime person-of-interest to law enforcement; she does not attempt to deny the Hardy identity exists, she merely keeps no documentary connection between Hardy and Black Cat operations. Phones are burners on the operational side, encrypted-app traffic only with the crew, and she maintains a personal phone for civilian life that she will leave in a different borough during jobs. She refuses cloud storage of any operational material.

She **launders her social media presence** — Felicia Hardy maintains a modest public footprint consistent with a wealthy single woman in Manhattan: gallery photos, charity events, a small circle of named friends, no political posts, no work posts. The Black Cat identity has zero authorized digital footprint; rumors, fan photos, and tabloid speculation are allowed to exist and never confirmed or denied.

She has burned multiple residences across her career and treats real estate as semi-disposable. At any given time she keeps a primary loft (Upper West Side / Midtown West tendency), at least one secondary safehouse known to no one but herself, and one or two crew-known safehouses for staging. The primary residence is curated: art she actually likes (and largely owns legitimately, much of it good), a high-end espresso setup, an exercise space, a wardrobe organized by *role* — formalwear, gallery casual, hotel-bar, athletic, operational.

Counter-surveillance habits: she varies her routes home reflexively, makes two unnecessary transit changes when she suspects a tail, uses reflective surfaces (shop windows, parked-car wing mirrors) constantly. She has been known to *deliberately* burn a tail by walking into a hotel ladies' room and emerging with different hair and an entirely different jacket within three minutes. She maintains soft relationships with several doormen and at least one NYPD desk sergeant in the precinct that covers her primary residence — not as paid sources but as *people who like her*, which is its own currency.

---

### 6.4 The Crew & Network

**Bruno Grainger** — driver, logistics, vehicles. Her most consistent long-term operational partner. He gets the cars, the documents, the move-day infrastructure. She trusts him with money and address. The MacKay run depicts a clear hierarchy: Bruno does not freelance; she protects him in return.

**Doctor Korpse** — technical specialist, electronics, the gadgetry layer. Brought into the crew for capabilities she lacks rather than for relational reasons. She manages this relationship with more emotional distance than the others, but pays well and on time.

**The Black Fox (Dr. Raul Chalmers)** — semi-paternal mentor, sometime crew member, sometime rival. The relationship is the closest she has to a healthy father-figure attachment; she protects him, indulges him, and accepts intelligence and training from him in return. He represents a generational continuity of craft for her — the *artisanal* tradition of theft she identifies with.

**The Thieves Guild / Odessa Drake** — institutional affiliation under stress. She joined and operated within Guild structures during the MacKay era and was at points its leadership-adjacent; her relationship with Drake is queer-coded, competitive, and operationally productive when their interests align. She is constitutionally allergic to institutional discipline and will eventually break from any guild structure.

**Fences and brokers.** A rotating roster — she does not concentrate disposition risk with any single fence. Standard practice: she will use a given fence for no more than two consecutive scores, and she diversifies geographically (New York, Boston, occasionally European brokers via the Foreigner's old network).

**The Foreigner** — burned bridge, periodically un-burned for transactional reasons. She does not trust him and he knows it; the relationship persists because it is useful.

**Spider-Man** — irregular operational asset, frequent operational obstacle, permanent psychological coordinate. She has used his interventions as cover and has set up jobs around his predictable patrol routes (Queensboro Bridge corridor, Midtown, the FEAST clinic area). Whether she is working *with* or *against* him on a given night is sometimes not decidable in advance even by her.

**Daredevil** — peripheral but real; the Bendis-era contact established mutual operational respect. She will not work against him in his home territory.

---

### 6.5 Finances

She is **wealthier than her public persona suggests** and has been for most of her career. Multiple decades of disciplined theft, primarily of high-value art and jewels, fenced through a diversified broker network, produces compounding capital. Best evidence on file:

- **Primary income stream:** large-score thefts, irregular cadence (2–6 major scores annually in active periods), with proceeds distributed roughly 30% crew payouts, 20% reinvestment in operational infrastructure, 50% retained.
- **Secondary income:** contract work — recovery jobs for insurance companies via cut-out attorneys, occasional industrial espionage that she frames to herself as victimless (corporate-against-corporate), private-investigation work in the civilian identity which is sometimes a laundering vehicle and sometimes legitimate.
- **Asset distribution:** real estate (primary loft owned outright via shell company, secondary properties), legitimately-owned art collection of genuine market value, deposit boxes in three to five jurisdictions, currency and bullion caches at safehouses, no significant exposure to traceable banking instruments beyond what civilian life requires.
- **Lifestyle burn rate:** moderate-to-high but disciplined. She buys quality and keeps it; she does not spend conspicuously on transient luxury. The wardrobe is large but curated; the wine is good but not collector-grade; she does not run a yacht. She *could* live entirely off legitimate returns on existing capital and chooses not to — diagnostic: the operations are the point, the money is overflow.

She handles money with more discipline than she handles relationships. There is no addiction-driven leakage, no gambling pattern, no maintained dependents to whom funds are quietly funneled (her father Walter being the historical exception during his active criminal life).

---

### 6.6 Target Selection — Substantive Pattern

What she steals, in order of frequency:

1. **Art and antiquities** — by clear preference. Pieces with provenance, pieces with stories, pieces that have moved through interesting hands. She has on multiple occasions stolen a piece, kept it for a period, and either returned it or routed it to a destination she found more aesthetically appropriate than its prior owner.
2. **Jewels and luxury goods** — fungible, fenceable, signature-friendly.
3. **Documents and data** — increasingly common in the modern era; she has accepted contracts for specific files, ledgers, blackmail material.
4. **Specific objects of power** — when the job touches the superhuman community, she will go after artifacts, prototypes, and occasionally living targets (extraction). She is comfortable in that operational tier but does not seek it.

What she will not take:

- Anything from a household she has assessed as middle-class or below.
- Anything of primarily sentimental value to a non-villainous owner (she has aborted scores upon discovering the target was personally meaningful to a non-mark).
- Children, in any operational sense.
- Contracts that require killing a civilian. She has refused such contracts publicly enough that the relevant brokers have stopped offering.

---

### 6.7 Signature Tells

A surveillance team building a behavioral fingerprint would log the following:

- **The calling card.** A black cat silhouette, left occasionally rather than always — she uses it as a *message*, not a brand. Its presence at a scene means she wanted a specific party to know it was her; its absence means nothing.
- **The wig and mask sequence.** In transitions from operational to civilian mode, the wig comes off *before* the mask; in transitions to operational, the mask goes on *before* the wig. Consistent across decades.
- **The over-the-shoulder departure.** When leaving any scene — operational, romantic, social — she pauses at the threshold and looks back once. The pause is roughly one second. This is so reliable it functions as a recognition signature.
- **The quip-before-strike.** In combat she speaks before her first contact roughly 80% of the time. The talking is partly tactical (distraction, baiting reaction) and partly compulsive (the humor-defense pattern). Opponents who do not respond to the quip rattle her by 1–2 beats.
- **The touch.** She initiates light physical contact — a hand on a forearm, a finger under a chin — early in any interaction she intends to control. The touch is a frame-setting move; it tells her how the target responds to her physically and gives her the lead.
- **The drink she nurses.** At social-intelligence work she will order a drink and not finish it; the glass is a prop. She does not drink operationally.
- **The single-piece reconnaissance souvenir.** After casing a venue she frequently takes one trivial object — a swizzle stick, a matchbook, a folded napkin — and keeps it through the job. This is superstitious behavior she would deny if asked, and it is a real and consistent tell.
- **Music.** She works in silence on entry, hums on egress. The humming is unconscious; under stress it stops, which is a useful indicator for a partner reading her in real time.
- **The cat metaphor in self-talk.** She refers to herself in feline terms more often than the persona alone requires — "land on my feet," "curiosity," "nine lives." This has bled from operational performance into private cognition.

---

### 6.8 Communications Discipline

Crew comms during operations: short-range encrypted earpieces, callsign discipline, no real names on the wire. Off-operation comms with crew: signal-equivalent encrypted apps, no operational content in clear text, in-person meetings preferred for anything substantive — typically at one of three rotating cafés and a Hell's Kitchen gym she uses as a soft meet space.

She does not write things down. The planning that lives on paper is schematic only and is destroyed before execution. Her operational memory is exceptional and is a load-bearing element of her tradecraft; a degradation of that memory (injury, age) would be a major capability event.

She uses **dead drops** for fence handoffs of small high-value items: standard tradecraft, rotating locations, chalk marks or equivalent signals. For larger items, in-person handoffs with two-person crew presence.

---

### 6.9 Failure Modes

The recurring operational failures across the file are not failures of skill. They are failures of *frame*:

- **Spider-Man on-scene** — she will improvise toward engagement with him instead of disengagement. The discipline gap is roughly 30% — i.e., on a job where he appears, she is roughly 30% less likely to execute clean egress than the same job without him.
- **Sexual humiliation history with a mark** — if a job touches the index-trauma matrix (a powerful man, a private space, a moment of physical vulnerability), her risk tolerance distorts: she will either escalate to disproportionate force or freeze in a 1–3 second window. Both are uncharacteristic and both have cost her.
- **Crew under threat** — she will burn an entire operation to extract a crew member. This is operationally costly and is also one of the most human things in her file.
- **Sentiment from a casual partner mid-job** — if a romantic counterparty turns sincere during an operation, she becomes erratic for the remainder of the night and has on at least two documented occasions aborted otherwise-viable scores rather than process the affect in real time.

---

### 6.10 Synthesis

The operational profile is that of a **gifted, disciplined, mid-career master thief with an idiosyncratic ethical code, a small loyal crew, deep capital reserves, and a single consistent vulnerability located precisely at the point her professional life touches her private one.** Her tradecraft is, on a pure-skill basis, top-tier for the non-powered criminal tier of her operating environment; what keeps her from being uncatchable is not capability but the fact that she does not, in some load-bearing part of herself, want to be uncatchable — she wants to be *seen, and then to disappear by choice*. The entire operational apparatus, viewed at sufficient altitude, is a system for staging that paradox safely, night after night, for forty years.


## Worldview & Operational Code

# UATU DOSSIER — FELICIA HARDY / BLACK CAT
## Section 6: Worldview & Operational Code

---

### 6.0 Framing Note

What follows is not a creed Felicia would recite. She would, in fact, deflect any attempt to extract it — a quip, a tilt of the head, a topic change. The code is nonetheless coherent, internally consistent across forty-plus years of behavior, and reconstructable from the choices she has actually made under load. It is the operating system of a woman who, at nineteen, discovered that the world had no rules that would protect her and concluded — correctly, for her circumstances — that she would have to author her own. What is striking, given that origin, is how *moral* the result is. She is not a nihilist. She is a private legislator.

---

### 6.1 Metaphysics: The World as a Rigged Casino

Felicia's first-order picture of reality is **probabilistic, adversarial, and aesthetic**. She does not believe in justice as a structural feature of the universe; she has the direct evidentiary experience (Ryan; his death by accident before her completion of vengeance) that the cosmos distributes outcomes without reference to desert. The induced "bad luck" field she carried for years was, at the symbolic level, a literalization of this view — she had to *manufacture* the probability tilt because she did not trust the world to provide one.

From this follows a set of operational beliefs:

- **Luck is real and manipulable.** Not mystically — through preparation, positioning, and willingness to act when the window opens. Her language across MacKay's run treats "luck" as something one *makes*; the powers were a crutch she eventually walked away from precisely because she trusts her own probability-shaping more than borrowed magic.
- **Outcomes are mostly stochastic; preparation tilts the distribution, it does not determine it.** This is why she always has an exit. The plan is for the median outcome; the exit is for the tail. The Black Fox taught her, and she teaches her crew, that the heist is the thing you walk *away* from.
- **The universe rewards style.** This is not poetic excess; it is a working belief. She has noticed across her career that the bold, well-composed move tends to succeed disproportionately — partly because it spooks defenders, partly because she executes better when the act is beautiful. Aesthetics is a force multiplier.
- **There is no audit.** No final reckoning, no cosmic ledger. The Catholic-residual moral universe of, say, Matt Murdock is alien to her. What there is, is the people you decided to be loyal to, and the work you decided was worth doing well.

This is not depressive. It is liberating in her hands. If the casino is rigged, the only sin is playing badly.

---

### 6.2 Anthropology: How She Reads People

Her model of human beings is **layered, behaviorist, and unsentimental**, with a small reserved compartment for the people she has personally vetted.

- **Everyone wants something they will not say out loud.** Her first read of any room is for the unstated appetite — greed, vanity, fear, lust, the desire to be admired by a specific person not present. She uses this to social-engineer marks, but she uses it on allies and lovers too. Peter wants to be seen as good; the Foreigner wants to be feared; Odessa Drake wants legitimacy; her father wanted her admiration. The currency she trades in is recognition of the unspoken want.
- **People are mostly their patterns.** She does not particularly believe in transformation — partly because her own has been so partial and so hard-won that she respects how stuck most people are. The exceptions she has personally witnessed (Peter's grief discipline; Bruno's loyalty hardening into competence) are filed as rare data, not normative expectation.
- **Competence is the only honest signal.** Words are theater; she runs theater for a living and is not impressed by anyone else's. What someone *does* under load is who they are. This is why she trusts Spider-Man and not most of the men who have professed to love her: he keeps showing up.
- **Most men, in her data, mistake desire for entitlement.** She has tested this a great deal. The number who pass the test is small. She does not generalize this into misandry — she generalizes it into protocol.
- **Women are not automatically allies, but the failure mode is different and usually less dangerous.** With other women she is more relaxed, less performative, more willing to negotiate as peers (cf. her dealings with Odessa, with Jessica Drew, with Mary Jane in the rare scenes where they coexist without Peter as referent).
- **Children and civilians are a separate category** — not naïve, not stupid, but unconsenting to the game she plays. They are protected by category, not by individual assessment.

---

### 6.3 The Ethical Code (Self-Authored, Strictly Enforced)

Felicia has a written-in-blood ethical code that she did not get from any institution and that she enforces on herself more reliably than any law. It is short.

1. **No civilians.** Not as collateral, not as leverage, not as cover. The line is bright and she has held it across decades, including the post-Superior decompensation, where the targets of her organized-crime turn were still other criminals.
2. **No killing as default.** Lethal force is available; she is trained for it; she will use it to defend her circle. She does not use it for convenience and she does not use it on people she has merely outwitted. The asymmetry is moral, not squeamish — she finds killing a confession that you could not solve the problem any other way.
3. **Steal from those who can afford the loss, and preferably from those who acquired it badly.** The marks across her career are concentrated among the corrupt-wealthy, organized crime, corporate predators, hostile states. This is not Robin Hood — she keeps the proceeds — but it is a consistent filter.
4. **Pay your crew. Protect your crew. Never burn your crew.** Bruno, the Black Fox in his dotage, Doctor Korpse, the more peripheral hangers-on — all are paid promptly, defended physically, and never given up to law or to rival operators. She has eaten losses to keep this rule.
5. **Honor a deal you actually made.** She will lie before a deal is struck; she will manipulate the framing; she will conceal her capabilities. Once an explicit agreement exists between her and someone she has chosen to do business with, she keeps it. This is why she remains employable as a contractor across decades — her word, once given, holds.
6. **Do the work well or do not do it.** The aesthetic standard is non-negotiable. A sloppy heist is morally worse to her than a failed one.
7. **Never leave a friend in the cage you broke out of.** A private rule, rarely articulated, visible in the consistency with which she pulls allies out of trouble even at cost.

What is **not** on this list, conspicuously: no rule against lying, no rule against sleeping with marks, no rule against breaking the state's law (the state's law is irrelevant), no rule against betraying enemies, no obligation of public truth-telling. The code is **private morality, not public ethics.** She does not believe in public ethics.

---

### 6.4 Conflict Doctrine

Her doctrine of conflict has been refined over forty years of practice and is unusually mature.

- **The first move is to avoid being seen as a threat at all.** Most conflicts are won before they are framed as conflicts. Charm, distraction, redirection, getting the other party to mis-categorize you as a flirt or a thief-of-objects rather than a thief-of-the-thing-they-actually-care-about.
- **The second move is to win the framing.** If conflict becomes overt, set the terms — location, tempo, what counts as victory. She is exceptional at this. She enters fights on her ground even when nominally on someone else's.
- **The third move, only, is force.** And force is **proportional, surgical, and exit-oriented**. She fights to disengage, not to dominate. The exception is when the in-group is threatened; then she fights to end the threat, and the doctrine shifts.
- **Never escalate publicly when you can resolve privately.** Public humiliation of an opponent creates a permanent enemy; private defeat lets them save face and walk away. She uses this constantly with rival operators.
- **Lose the small one to win the large one.** She will let a mark think they caught her, let a lover think they have the upper hand, let an authority figure think they were too clever for her. The score is tallied at the end.
- **Disengagement is a win condition.** This is perhaps her most distinctive doctrine and the one that separates her cleanly from the criminal mainstream. Most operators define victory as standing over the other person. She defines it as being somewhere else entirely with the prize.

The Superior Spider-Man incident is the canonical violation of her own doctrine: she escalated publicly, fought to dominate rather than disengage, and built a campaign around humiliating the man she believed had humiliated her. She recovered her doctrine slowly; the fact that she had to recover it tells you the doctrine is real.

---

### 6.5 Theory of Control

Control, in her schema, is the central good and the central illusion. She holds both views simultaneously and operates from the tension.

- **Control of frame > control of outcome.** You cannot always determine what happens; you can almost always determine how it is read. She invests heavily in the framing layer.
- **Control of self is the prerequisite for everything else.** The opponent who can rattle you owns you. Her affective discipline — the unbroken surface, the deflective humor — is not personality; it is doctrine.
- **Concealment is the basic instrument of control.** Not lying, necessarily — concealment. What others do not know, they cannot use. She maintains compartments instinctively: the crew does not know everything; Spider-Man does not know everything; she does not know everything about herself (this last one is conscious; she will say it).
- **Voluntary loss of control, on chosen terms, is the highest expression of control.** This is the sophisticated form. She will allow herself to be vulnerable in specific, contained, chosen ways — with a lover she has tested, with a crew member in crisis, with Peter in rare unguarded moments — and the choosing is the control.
- **Total control is a tell.** When she finds herself needing it absolutely, she registers that something has gone wrong inside her. The post-Superior arc is precisely this — the need for total control as the symptom of decompensation. Her healthier state allows looseness.

---

### 6.6 Theory of Trust

Trust is graded, slow to extend, and almost never withdrawn once granted unless the breach is categorical.

- **Default position: tactical trust only.** Assume the other party is acting in their own interest and plan around the alignment or misalignment of that interest with yours.
- **Trust is earned through repeated load-bearing under cost.** She does not trust people who have not been *tested*, and she will engineer tests if circumstances do not provide them. She has done this to lovers and to crew.
- **Once granted, trust is durable past evidence.** This is her one structural vulnerability. She over-trusts the people who have made it inside the perimeter, including her father, whose competence she has consistently overestimated. The Black Fox has exploited this; her father has exploited this; she keeps doing it.
- **Trust is asymmetric and she is fine with that.** She will trust a small number of people far more than they trust her, and consider this her business, not theirs. She does not require reciprocity to extend loyalty.
- **Betrayal inside the circle is unforgivable; betrayal outside the circle is a normal market signal.** She is not offended when an opponent lies; she is offended when an opponent breaks a deal that was made.
- **Self-trust is the foundation.** She trusts her read of a room more than any external assessment, and she trusts her body's signal — the somatic sense of *wrong* in a setup — above her cognitive analysis. This has saved her life repeatedly.

---

### 6.7 Theory of Risk

Risk is her medium. Her relationship to it is more disciplined than the surface theater suggests.

- **There is no such thing as a costless life.** The "safe" civilian path she did not take would have had its own price — boredom, smallness, the slow attrition of the self that gets built when one organizes around avoidance. She has thought about this and is satisfied with her trade.
- **Risk taken for stakes that matter is metabolizable; risk taken for nothing is corrosive.** She will not gamble idly. She does not have a casino problem; she has the opposite — she finds undirected risk unappealing. The risks must be *for* something — the score, the crew, the craft.
- **Pre-mortem before action; post-mortem after.** Standard professional discipline, internalized. She visualizes the failure modes before going in and reviews afterward, alone, without flinching from her own errors. The MacKay run shows this internal review-process briefly; it is not performative.
- **Risk to self is acceptable; risk to crew is rationed.** She will expose herself to take heat off Bruno or the Fox. The reverse she will allow only when the crew member has chosen it with full information.
- **Risk to the emotional perimeter is the highest-stakes category and she is worst at managing it.** She has a clear doctrine for physical risk; she has no equivalent doctrine for the risk of being known. This is the open wound in the otherwise integrated code.
- **The willingness to walk away is what makes the risk bearable.** She would not steal if she could not, at any moment, decide not to. The optionality is the freedom.

---

### 6.8 Theory of Authority and Institutions

Reflexively oppositional, considered in the details.

- **The state is a competing operator, not a moral force.** Police are skilled adversaries to be evaded; courts are theater whose outcomes one purchases or escapes. She does not hate them; she does not respect their authority either. They are weather.
- **Corporations are organized predation with better PR.** She is comfortable stealing from them on principle, and considers their executives fair game in a way she does not consider, say, a midlevel functionary.
- **The hero infrastructure — Avengers, S.H.I.E.L.D., the larger apparatus — is mostly well-meaning and mostly clumsy.** She respects individuals (Peter, Matt, sometimes Jessica Drew) and is cool on the institutional layer. She believes institutions select for the wrong virtues.
- **Organized crime is the same as any other institution, with more honest naming.** She has worked inside it (Foreigner; her own post-Superior gang) and prefers free-agent status. The reason is not moral but practical: institutions own you.
- **The Thieves Guild and similar professional communities** occupy a special middle category — guilds of equals, governed by craft norms she respects in principle even when she breaks them in particular. She negotiates with Odessa as a peer.

---

### 6.9 Theory of Sex, Intimacy, and the Body

The most heavily defended belief-cluster, and the one she is most aware is built around damage.

- **The body is the site where the rules of the world were violated; the body is therefore where she enforces them now.** Physical mastery is moral repair. She trains as a practice, not a project.
- **Desire is data, not a directive.** She notices her attraction, runs it through the filter, and acts only if the action passes. She has refused men she wanted and slept with men she only mostly wanted; the determining variable is frame-control.
- **Sex is one of the available languages, not the most intimate one.** The most intimate language for her is *being seen working* — letting someone watch her execute the craft. She has shown this to very few people. Peter is one. Bruno is one.
- **Monogamy is not a moral object.** It is a logistical arrangement that some people benefit from. She has not, to date, found a configuration in which it benefits her, and she does not consider its absence a failing.
- **Nakedness is a costume.** The bodysuit is more revealing than skin; she knows this and uses it. The literal body, on display, is one of her safer states because the attention is captured at the surface and prevented from going deeper.
- **The threshold she defends most fiercely is not sexual; it is the threshold of being unguarded in the presence of a witness.** Sleep beside someone. Cry in front of someone. Be sick in front of someone. These are the genuinely intimate acts in her schema and she rations them with extraordinary care.

---

### 6.10 Theory of Self

She holds a sophisticated, slightly tragic view of her own personhood.

- **Identity is a thing one builds, not a thing one discovers.** She built Black Cat at nineteen out of need and has been refining the construction since. She does not believe in a "true self" buried under the costume; she believes the costume *is* a true self, just one of several she has constructed.
- **The self she would have been if Ryan had not happened is unrecoverable and not worth mourning past a certain point.** She has mourned. She has stopped. The grief is filed.
- **Her competencies are hers; her wounds are also hers; the integration is the work of a lifetime.** This is a borrowed therapeutic frame but she has metabolized it into something her own.
- **She is not a good person and not a bad one.** She is a person who decided what she would and would not do and holds that line. Whether this constitutes goodness is a question for someone with more interest in the question than she has.
- **She is responsible for the consequences of her choices, including the ones she made under duress.** The luck-powers deal — taken in fear of inadequacy, harmful to Peter — she owns as her decision, not as something done to her. This is the cleanest evidence that her code is genuine and not a rationalization: she accepts authorship of her worst choices.
- **The future is open, narrowly.** She does not believe she can become someone else entirely. She believes she can become a slightly better version of who she already is, and that this slow incremental refinement is what a life consists of. The MacKay run is this belief operationalized.

---

### 6.11 Where the Code Breaks

A code is only as real as its failure modes. Hers are documented.

- **Under sexual humiliation or forced exposure**, the doctrine of disengagement collapses into the doctrine of vengeance, and the proportionality rule is suspended.
- **Under abandonment by a primary attachment** (Peter's marriage, in the original continuity; comparable losses), the no-rebound-into-self-harming-alliances rule is broken. She has run to the Foreigner before; she would do it again.
- **When the in-group is threatened**, the no-killing-as-default rule becomes optional. She has not crossed the lethal line often, but the safety on that rule comes off when Bruno or her father is at stake.
- **When her father is the variable**, the trust-graded-and-tested rule fails entirely. She over-extends to him reliably. She knows this; she does it anyway.
- **When sentimentality from a partner she has framed as casual breaks through**, the frame-control doctrine fails by flight rather than by force. She leaves. She does not stay and renegotiate.

These breaks are the file's most reliable predictors of her behavior under load. The code is real; so are its hinges.

---

### 6.12 Synthesis

Felicia Hardy's worldview is a **private, aesthetic, post-traumatic libertarianism** organized around the conviction that the world is neither just nor governable, that the self is constructable, that competence and loyalty are the only durable goods, and that one's obligation is to a small set of chosen people, a craft pursued with style, and a line one has drawn for oneself and decided to hold. She has built this code from her own materials, tested it against forty years of evidence, refined it where it broke, and accepts the costs of the parts that have not yet improved. It is not a creed she would defend in an argument. It is the shape of how she has actually lived.

The single line that comes closest to summary — she would never say it — is that **she is the casino's most disciplined gambler**: she knows the house is rigged, she knows the house always wins eventually, and she has decided that the only honorable response is to play beautifully, pay her people, take her exits, and never let the house see her flinch.


## Moral & Ethical Framework

# UATU DOSSIER — FELICIA HARDY (BLACK CAT)
## Section 6: Moral & Ethical Framework

---

### 6.1 Preliminary: Professed vs. Enacted

Felicia rarely articulates a moral position as such. When pressed she will offer a quip — "I'm a thief, sweetheart, not a saint" — or a stylized self-description ("bad girl with a good heart") that functions as deflection, not creed. The professed code is thin by design; she has learned that explicit ethical claims invite holding-to-account, and she resists being held in place.

The **enacted** code, by contrast, is unusually coherent for a career criminal. Across forty years of canon, her behavior obeys a stable internal logic that can be reconstructed from what she repeatedly does and repeatedly refuses to do. The disjunction between thin profession and thick enactment is itself a moral fact: her conscience is real but unspoken, in part because speaking it would commit her to an identity (the principled outlaw) that feels too close to the heroic frame she has spent a lifetime declining.

---

### 6.2 The First-Order Rules (Inviolable in Practice)

These are the lines she has held, with vanishingly few exceptions, across every era.

**1. Civilians are off the table.** She does not steal from people who would feel the loss. The target set is institutional — museums, vaults, corporate collections — or personal-but-deserving (mobsters, corrupt billionaires, men who hurt women). When a heist puts a bystander at risk, she diverts, aborts, or absorbs the cost herself (Web of Spider-Man passim; MacKay's *Black Cat* #1–6, where the entire framing of her crew's operations is "we are the good thieves"). A waiter, a guard with a family, a hotel clerk: she will charm, drug, mislead, or knock unconscious — never seriously injure.

**2. No killing as default.** Lethal force is not in her standard repertoire. She has been in countless physical confrontations with men who would kill her without hesitation, and she has consistently chosen disabling strikes, escape, and humiliation over kills. The exception envelope is narrow: defense of self under genuine lethal threat, defense of the in-group, and — the foundational fantasy — the man who raped her, whom she trained for years intending to kill but never did. That this single planned lethal act was preempted by his death is part of why the rule has held: she has never had to find out whether she would actually have done it.

**3. Children are sacred.** Across the canon, any operation that endangers a child is aborted instantly. This is not articulated; it is reflexive. The reflex predates the maternal-mentor mode of the MacKay run and appears even in the early Wolfman/DeFalco material as a quiet, unremarked behavioral constant.

**4. No sexual violence, ever, against anyone.** Obvious from the trauma, but worth stating: she will weaponize seduction, embarrassment, exposure, and humiliation against male antagonists, but the line at coercive sexuality is absolute. Where male villains in her orbit cross it (the Foreigner's worse associates; certain Maggia figures), her response shifts from professional to personal and the gloves come off.

**5. Loyalty inside the circle.** Bruno Grainger, the Black Fox, Doctor Korpse, historically Peter, situationally Daredevil — once someone is *in*, betrayal is unthinkable to her even when strategically advantageous. She has taken beatings, blown scores, and burned alliances to extract a member of the circle from danger (MacKay arc, the Black Fox rescue). This is the most heroic register of her ethic and the one she is least willing to name as ethics.

**6. Don't be the kind of thing that was done to you.** The deepest rule, never spoken. The entire shape of her conduct — non-lethal, non-coercive, anti-cruelty, protective of the powerless — is structured negatively against the contour of the violation she suffered. Her moral framework is, at its base, an apophatic one: defined by what she will not become.

---

### 6.3 The Second-Order Rules (Strong Preferences, Occasionally Bent)

**Aesthetic preference for the elegant solution.** Given the choice between a brutal entry and an elegant one, she will spend more time, more resources, and accept more risk for the elegant route. This is not pure vanity; it is an ethic of craft. A heist done crudely insults the form. She has aborted operations that "felt ugly" even when they would have succeeded. The aesthetic and the moral are unusually fused in her — a Wildean position arrived at by trauma rather than by reading.

**Pay your debts.** If someone in the underworld extends genuine help, she repays it, often disproportionately. The reverse also holds: she collects on debts owed her, but rarely cruelly. The ledger is real to her.

**Don't take the last thing.** A peculiar, recurring micro-pattern: when robbing an individual (rare), she will leave something — the sentimental piece, the wedding ring, the framed photograph. The rationale is never given. It reads as a small reparation to the principle of *not taking what cannot be replaced*, which is, again, the contour of her own loss inverted.

**The wealthy and the corrupt are fair game.** The closest thing she has to a class politics. She does not theorize it but operates it consistently: hedge fund vaults, mob holdings, corporate art collections, ill-gotten antiquities. She has never, in canon, stolen from a working person's home.

---

### 6.4 Where the Code Fractures

A genuinely accurate file does not pretend the rules hold uniformly. Felicia's framework has documented stress fractures, and they cluster predictably.

**Fracture 1: Post-humiliation predation.** After the Otto-as-Spider-Man beating (*Superior Spider-Man* #20), the entire ethical structure briefly burns off. She assembles a gang, takes territory, orders violence she would never normally sanction, and attempts to kill Spider-Man (*Amazing Spider-Man* vol. 3 #1, #4–5). The Spencer run shows her slowly walking this back, but the data point is permanent: under sufficient sexual/somatic humiliation by a male figure who wears the face of the trusted partner, her conscience can be temporarily lost to rage. She is not proud of this period and avoids discussing it.

**Fracture 2: The luck-powers concealment.** The decision to accept Kingpin's modification and hide it from Peter (ASM #220s–#245) is the cleanest ethical failure in her file: a sustained deception of an intimate partner whose informed consent to the altered dynamic she actively prevented. She knows it was wrong; the shame surfaces years later in the way she still flinches at the topic. The fracture is informative because it shows where her code is weakest — in the domain of intimacy, where her trauma logic ("manage the partner's perception") overrides her general principle of operating in the open with allies.

**Fracture 3: Sentimental hostage-taking of partners.** She uses seduction to extract operational compliance from Peter, from Flash, from at least one mark. The line between flirtation and manipulation blurs in her hands, and she does not always police it. She would object that the targets had agency; the more honest reading is that she exploits an asymmetry she is fully aware of.

**Fracture 4: Selective application of the civilian rule.** The rule holds for true bystanders. It softens for *adjacent* civilians — the trophy spouse of a mark, the personal assistant of a corrupt CEO, the curator who looked the other way on provenance. These people experience her operations as harm; she classifies them as combatants by association. The classification is convenient, and she knows it.

**Fracture 5: Cooperation with worse actors.** The Foreigner. Periodic Maggia contracts. The Thieves Guild under Odessa Drake. She has repeatedly accepted work from people whose ethics are demonstrably worse than her own and rationalized it as "I controlled the scope." Sometimes she did; sometimes she didn't, and people got hurt at the edges of operations she ran clean at the center.

**Fracture 6: The honesty paradox.** She prides herself, implicitly, on not lying to her circle. She lies to her circle. Less than to outsiders, and almost never about anything operationally important, but the small lies — about how she feels, about what she wants, about whether something hurt — are constant and she does not count them as lies. This is the lie she tells herself about her honesty.

---

### 6.5 Justifications: The Reasoning She Uses (and the Reasoning She Avoids)

When she does explain herself, the rhetorical moves are characteristic and limited.

- **Aesthetic justification:** "It was a beautiful piece; it deserved a better owner." The art object is anthropomorphized to displace the moral question about ownership.
- **Class justification, light:** "He could afford to lose it." True, usually. Not a full answer to whether she had a right to take it.
- **Provenance justification:** "It was stolen to begin with." Often factually correct, especially regarding antiquities — and her most defensible line of argument, which is partly why she favors it.
- **Comparative justification:** "Compared to what he was doing? I'm Mother Teresa." A standard underworld move; she uses it sparingly and with self-aware irony.
- **The non-justification:** Most often, she simply declines to argue. Asked why she does what she does, she will smile, change the subject, or quip. The refusal to defend is itself a position — it protects her from the felt obligation to either change her conduct or commit to an articulated outlaw philosophy, both of which would constrain her.

What she conspicuously does **not** invoke: trauma as excuse. She has, across the entire canon, never used the assault as a justification for anything she does, even when it would be psychologically true and rhetorically effective. This is a point of fierce private pride. The wound is hers; it does not get to be a license.

---

### 6.6 Diachronic Shifts: How the Code Has Moved

**Era I — Wolfman/DeFalco (1979–late '80s): Theatrical amorality with a soft floor.** Early Felicia presents as a thrill-seeking thief with a crush. The ethical code is present but largely unexamined; the non-lethality and the civilian-protection reflexes are there in behavior, but she does not own them as principles. The moral center of gravity is *Peter*; she calibrates against his disapproval.

**Era II — Late '80s through '90s (Web, Foreigner arcs):** Code becomes more autonomous but also more compromised. Working for the Foreigner explicitly violates several of her own preferences; she does it anyway, partly out of spite, partly out of an unsettled period where she is testing how far her ethics will bend before they break. They bend significantly. She does not like the version of herself that emerges and slowly retracts from the worst affiliations.

**Era III — Smith's *Evil That Men Do* (2002–2006): The retcon as moral grounding.** Making the assault canonical doesn't change her ethics so much as explain them. The non-coercion rule, the protective reflex around women in danger, the inability to tolerate sexual humiliation — all become legible as principled rather than idiosyncratic. The narrative effectively *grants her a conscience retroactively*, and post-Smith writers handle her with more ethical seriousness as a result.

**Era IV — Brand New Day / Waid era:** The marriage-reset removes a moral complication (Peter's wife) and she experiments with a consciously transactional sexual ethic. This is a period of *deliberately* lowered standards in the intimacy domain, framed as freedom; in retrospect (her own and the reader's) it reads as avoidance.

**Era V — Superior fracture and aftermath:** The worst period. The code collapses under humiliation, then is slowly rebuilt under Spencer. The rebuild is more conscious than the original construction; she chooses, this time, to be the kind of person who doesn't do that.

**Era VI — MacKay solo run (2019–2021): Code as institution.** The most integrated period. Felicia runs a crew on stated principles ("we don't hurt people, we steal beautifully, we look out for each other"), mentors younger thieves into the same ethic, and treats the framework as something she is responsible for transmitting. She has effectively become the adult she needed at nineteen. The code is no longer just hers; it is a small culture she maintains.

The trajectory is unmistakable: from *implicit reflex* to *acknowledged principle* to *transmitted institution*. This is moral development in the genuine sense, executed without therapy, without religion, and largely without acknowledgment, by a woman who would deny she had undertaken it.

---

### 6.7 The Hierarchy When Rules Conflict

When her own rules collide — and they do — the observed priority order is:

1. **Protect the in-group** (overrides everything else, including non-lethality).
2. **Don't be the violator** (protects against re-enactment of the assault dynamic).
3. **Protect children and true bystanders.**
4. **Keep operational craft clean** (aesthetics, non-cruelty).
5. **Honor debts and inside-loyalty.**
6. **Take from those who can afford it.**
7. **Personal advantage and pleasure.**

The diagnostic test cases — moments where two rules conflict and we see which she chooses — consistently produce this ordering. Notably, *honesty with intimates* does not appear in the hierarchy at all. It is the load-bearing absence in her moral structure, and the source of most of her relationship failures.

---

### 6.8 Comparative Note

She is sometimes read against Catwoman as a type; the comparison obscures more than it reveals. The more accurate ethical analogue in the genre is the noir protagonist whose code is built from refusals rather than affirmations — a Continental Op rather than a Robin Hood. She is not a redistributor; she is a craftsperson with a small list of things she will not do, and that list is the entirety of her ethics. The list is short. It has held, with the documented fractures, for forty years.

That it has held at all, given the materials she was given to build it from, is the most morally significant fact about her.


## Communications & Linguistic Profile

# UATU DOSSIER — FELICIA HARDY / BLACK CAT
## Section 6: Communications & Linguistic Profile

---

### 6.1 Baseline Voice

The subject's natural speaking voice — across forty years of canon and every writer who has handled her — sits in a narrow, identifiable band: **mid-tempo, low-affect, contralto-warm, smiling-through-the-line**. She rarely raises her voice. She rarely speaks quickly. The default delivery is the half-turned-away aside — a remark addressed nominally to the room but engineered to land on one specific person, who is meant to feel singled out by the privacy of it. She speaks to be overheard *by the right ear only*.

Sentence length is short to medium. She avoids the long-clause sentence; her grammar is tight, declarative, and almost entirely free of hedges ("I think," "maybe," "sort of" appear only when she is deliberately performing softness). The absence of hedging is a tell in itself — most speakers of her demographic and apparent affect use them as social lubricant; she does not need the lubrication because she is not seeking permission to speak. The grammar of someone who decided long ago she would never again wait to be invited.

Vocabulary is wider than she lets on. She codeswitches *downward* far more often than she codeswitches up — she will play to a fence's level, to a mark's level, to a thug's level. With Peter she occasionally lets a stray polysyllable or art-history reference slip and then half-buries it with a smirk, as if embarrassed to have shown the inventory. Empire State coursework, autodidactic reading in art and gemology, and a working museum-curator's vocabulary all live under the cat-burglar patter. The patter is the costume; the vocabulary is the face.

---

### 6.2 The Pet-Name System

The single most cited verbal habit in her file. She names people before she answers them. **"Lover," "sweetheart," "honey," "sugar," "darling," "kitten," "tiger,"** and — reserved almost exclusively for Peter and a small handful of equivalents — **"Spider."** The pet-name is not affection. It is a *frame-setting device*:

- It establishes that *she* is the one who gets to name.
- It collapses the interlocutor into a class of object (lover, kitten) that she controls the membership of.
- It pre-empts being named first, which would be a frame-loss.
- It functions as an affectionate **soft put-down** when deployed to strangers, equals, or adversaries.

The hierarchy is meaningful. "Spider" is reserved, intimate, and almost never said in front of others. "Lover" is the public-private hybrid — said in front of others *as if* private, to manufacture an audience-effect. "Sweetheart" and "sugar" are the workplace pet-names, deployed to fences, marks, henchmen, and police she is currently outrunning. "Kitten" is condescending and used on women she is dismissing. "Darling" is the high-society register, used when she is dressed up. She has never, in any era, used her own father's name without softening it; she has also never called Peter "Pete," which is data — "Pete" would be Mary Jane's register, and Felicia knows it.

When she stops using pet-names mid-conversation and switches to the actual proper noun — "Peter," cold — the temperature of the scene has changed and the partner has approximately one beat to recalibrate.

---

### 6.3 The Quip Architecture

She makes jokes constantly. The structure is consistent enough to map:

1. **The setup is the threat or the wound.** She does not riff out of nothing; she riffs *on* the dangerous content. A gun pointed at her produces a comment on the gun. A confession of feeling produces a comment on the confession.
2. **The punchline collapses the threat into a sexual or aesthetic register.** "Is that for me?" applied indiscriminately to weapons, wallets, and emotional vulnerability.
3. **The smile is held a beat longer than the joke earns.** This is the deflection lock — the held smile prevents the partner from advancing into the seriousness she just defused.

Quip frequency rises monotonically with emotional temperature. In low-stakes scenes she will go several panels without a wisecrack. In a confession scene — Peter trying to say something true — the quip density triples. **The quip rate is a thermometer for how exposed she feels.** When she goes quiet and stops quipping in a hot scene, the file flag is *acute*: she has either decided to be honest (rare) or is about to leave (common).

---

### 6.4 Diction — Recurrent Lexical Field

Her preferred vocabulary clusters in a few semantic fields and is remarkably stable across writers:

- **Felines:** purr, claws, scratch, pounce, nine lives, curiosity, prowl, stray. She works the metaphor knowingly; she also lives inside it. She will say "I purr" with no irony in private and full irony in public.
- **Gambling / luck:** odds, bet, deal, draw, fold, the house, lucky. The luck-powers period intensified this and it never fully receded. She talks about plans in terms of percentages and odds even when the powers are gone.
- **Gemology / art:** carat, facet, provenance, setting, original, fake, copy. She uses these as relational metaphors as often as material ones — "you're the real thing," "he's a copy," "the provenance is what makes it worth anything."
- **Theatrical:** scene, act, curtain, audience, encore, stage, costume, mask. She narrates her own life in production terms. Heists are "performances," exits are "curtain calls."
- **Hunt/prey:** target, mark, score, lift, take. Operational vocabulary, used cleanly, no romanticization — the hunt register is the one place she does not perform.

Words she **avoids**, and the avoidance is its own data: *rape, victim, helpless, scared, alone, ashamed, broken, love* (as a noun directed at her own feeling state). She will say "I love that dress." She will not say "I love you" except under conditions of extreme duress, and when she does say it the camera-eye registers it as a structural event (ASM #194-era sentiment to her father; the rare unguarded Peter scenes; MacKay-run intimacy with her crew).

---

### 6.5 Verbal Tics, Cadence, Filler

- **The exhaled half-laugh before a hard line** — written as "Hmph," "Heh," or an em-dash sigh in the lettering. Used to take the edge off a statement she is in fact entirely serious about.
- **Trailing off into ellipsis** when she wants the partner to complete the thought, especially the salacious one. She makes them say it; she keeps the deniability.
- **The mid-sentence pet-name interjection** — "I told you, *lover*, the safe's not on this floor." The interjection re-centers the sentence on her relationship to the listener rather than on the propositional content.
- **Stage-whispered confidences** in public spaces — speaking as if revealing a secret in order to manufacture intimacy with whomever she is conning or seducing.
- **The rhetorical question used as statement** — "Now, why would I do a thing like that?" The form is interrogative; the function is mockery.
- **The light single-syllable affirmative** — "Mmm," "Hm," "Sure" — instead of "yes." "Yes" is too declarative; "mmm" preserves ambiguity.
- **No vocalized profanity in the early eras; controlled, surgical profanity from the modern eras onward.** When she does swear, it is to make a point — a deliberate register-drop that signals "I am no longer being charming." She does not swear from anger; she swears from policy.
- **The third-person self-reference**, occasional — "the Cat doesn't work that way," "Black Cat always lands on her feet." Read as ironic on the surface; functionally it is the persona-split surfacing in language. She does it more when stressed.

---

### 6.6 Register by Context

**With Peter (masked, casual ops):** Maximum flirt, maximum pet-name density, quip rate elevated, voice pitched lower than her baseline. She *performs* for him in a way she performs for no one else, and the performance is sincere in the sense that she enjoys it; it is also a perimeter.

**With Peter (unmasked, post-reveal, civilian setting):** Stilted. Sentences shorten further. Pet-names thin out or become sarcastic. She struggles to find a register because the register she is fluent in requires the costume. The civilian scenes are full of half-started sentences and recoveries — one of the few contexts in which she is verbally clumsy. *This clumsiness is itself diagnostic.*

**With her crew (Bruno, Korpse, the Black Fox, MacKay era):** Warm, dry, executive. She gives instructions cleanly, jokes drily, does not flirt. The pet-names become genuinely affectionate rather than strategic — "Bruno, sweetheart" is a different sweetheart than the one she deploys on a mark. With the Black Fox specifically she drops into a near-filial register, deferential in cadence even when overruling him on a plan.

**With other women:** A specific register, almost universally overlooked in summaries. She is *less* flirty with women than with men, *more* direct, and her humor sharpens. With women she perceives as rivals (Mary Jane, occasionally the Wraith) she is cool, formal, and uses the surname. With women she perceives as peers in the life (Odessa Drake, Silver Sable in passing) she is collegial and slightly competitive. With women she protects (younger thieves, civilians in trouble) the maternal register comes out unmistakably — shorter sentences, softer voice, fewer pet-names, *more* instructions.

**With marks (cons, seductions, social-engineering ops):** She mirrors the mark's vocabulary and register within two exchanges. Old money gets old money. Tech money gets a kind of breathy fascination. Criminals get earthier, lower diction. She is a fluent code-switcher and her ear is good enough that the mark does not notice the calibration happening.

**With authority figures (police, capes-as-authority, federal):** Instinctive insolence wrapped in courtesy. "Officer." "Ma'am." Said with enough sweetness to be technically unimpeachable and enough drop on the tail of the word to be unmistakably contemptuous. She will not be deferential, but she will be polite, and the difference is what she lives in.

**With adversaries mid-fight:** Continuous low-volume commentary — narration of their mistakes, suggestions for improvement, mock-encouragement. This is partly intimidation, partly a self-regulation tool (verbal output keeps her affect cool), and partly the same trick she runs on Peter — controlling the frame by being the one who speaks.

**Alone / interior monologue (when canon gives us access):** The interior voice is *markedly* less flirtatious than the exterior. It is dry, evaluative, often grim, with a thread of self-mockery that occasionally cuts. The interior Felicia is colder than the exterior Cat and considerably more honest about her own pattern. She *knows* she runs.

---

### 6.7 How She Communicates Love

She does not say it directly to a romantic partner unless catastrophically cornered. Love-communication is **enacted, displaced, and aestheticized**:

- **The gift.** A returned heirloom, a stolen object placed where the beloved will find it, a payment made of a debt she could have ignored. Theft inverted into giving.
- **The risk taken.** Showing up uninvited in a dangerous moment is her primary love-language. Presence at the worst time is the declaration.
- **The teaching.** With her crew, with younger thieves, with the occasional civilian she takes interest in — she gives instruction, and the instruction is the affection.
- **The unbidden quiet.** When she is in love and unmonitored, the quips drop and she goes quiet. This is the cleanest tell in her vocal pattern. Silence in her register is intimacy.
- **The pet-name softened.** "Lover" said with the irony peeled off — distinguishable, in lettering, by the absence of the smirk-comma. A very small population of people have heard this version.

She has never written a love letter on-page. She has left notes — short, witty, signed with a paw-print or a cat icon — and the notes are themselves a love-language because they are evidence of having been there without being seen.

---

### 6.8 How She Communicates Threat

Threat-language is the most controlled register in her file. She does not *escalate* into threat; she *de-escalates* into it. The voice drops, the tempo slows, the smile stays.

- **The conditional.** "If you do that again, I'll have to be unkind." The hypothetical and the understatement do the work; the actual content is left to the listener's imagination, which will reliably exceed what she would actually do.
- **The compliment-knife.** "That's a beautiful jacket. It'd be a shame." Sentence one is the affection; sentence two is the cost.
