- **The use of the second person possessive about the listener's body.** "Your hand. Your knee. Your jaw." Naming a body part is naming where the next contact will be.
- **The pet-name retained.** She threatens with "sweetheart" still in the sentence — the dissonance is the menace. The moment she drops the pet-name and uses the proper noun, the threat has already become an action and the talking phase is over.
- **The silence.** When she stops speaking entirely in a confrontation, the partner should be assumed to be in immediate physical danger.

She does not bluster. She does not list capabilities. She does not invoke allies. The threat-style is the threat-style of someone who has done it before and does not need the listener to believe her in advance.

---

### 6.9 How She Communicates Grief

She does not, in any register accessible to most observers. Grief-language in her file is **conspicuous by replacement**:

- **Activity-displacement.** A heist within forty-eight hours of a major loss. The plan-talk replaces the grief-talk.
- **Sex as eulogy.** Documented across multiple arcs — she metabolizes loss through a physical encounter with someone *other* than the lost figure. The act is the speech.
- **The single-line acknowledgment, dropped flat, followed by subject change.** "He's gone. — Anyway." The em-dash is doing structural labor; the "anyway" is the lid going back on.
- **The drink raised without a toast spoken.** A recurring image. The unspoken toast is the eulogy.
- **The visit to a place.** Father's grave, Empire State campus, the rooftop of a past meeting. She does not speak at these locations; she stands. The pilgrimage is the language.

When grief does break through verbally — Smith's *Evil That Men Do*, the immediate aftermath of the Otto incident, the rare losses inside her crew — the register that surfaces is *anger*, not sadness. Vocabulary spikes for revenge, for hunting, for owing. She does not have a fluent grammar of sadness because she never built one; the grief was triaged at nineteen and the file has been running on the workaround ever since.

---

### 6.10 Deflection Vocabulary

A short catalogue of phrases that recur across writers and that mark the moment she is dodging something true:

- "Don't be boring."
- "Are we doing this now?"
- "Mm — I don't do that conversation."
- "Save it, lover."
- "Ask me again when you've earned it."
- "Maybe in another life."
- "You don't want to know."
- "Buy me a drink first."

Each of these is a closing move. Each preserves charm. Each forecloses follow-up. Trained interlocutors learn to recognize them as the wall; untrained interlocutors mistake them for invitations to flirt and never get past them.

---

### 6.11 Written Communication

Sparse on-panel record, but consistent. Short. Handwritten when possible — she has a fine, slanted, slightly old-fashioned cursive, the by-product of a Catholic-school-grade penmanship education that intersects oddly with the cat-burglar persona. She signs with a paw-print, a cat silhouette, or — at maximum intimacy — her initial. Never her full signature on anything that could be evidence. Digital communication is sparing, encrypted, and tonally identical to her speech: short, dry, pet-name on the open, ellipsis on the close.

---

### 6.12 Master Tells — Linguistic

For analysts working live transcript or live audio, the highest-signal markers:

1. **Quip rate spike** — she is uncomfortable; map what was just said.
2. **Quip rate collapse to zero in a hot scene** — she is about to be honest *or* about to leave; the next thirty seconds decide which.
3. **Pet-name dropped, proper noun substituted** — the affective frame just changed; treat as escalation in either direction (intimacy or threat).
4. **Third-person self-reference** — persona-split surfacing under stress.
5. **Stray polysyllable / art reference** — she is comfortable enough to forget the patter; she is, in this moment, accessible.
6. **Held smile past the joke** — defense lock engaged; do not push.
7. **Verbal clumsiness, half-started sentences** — she is out of register, which means she is out of armor; the rarest and most diagnostic state in the file.

The throughline: Felicia Hardy speaks as someone who decided, at nineteen, that she would never again be made to say something she had not chosen to say. Every habit above descends from that decision. The voice is the lock; the silences are the key; and the only people who have ever heard the unlocked register are the very small number of people she has, briefly, allowed to.


## Predictive Model I — Routine & Social

# UATU DOSSIER — FELICIA HARDY
## Section 6: Predictive Model I — Routine & Social

A behavioral prediction grid for everyday situations the canon never depicted. Each entry is derived from the substantiated patterns in Sections 1–5: PTSD-organized compensation, frame-control imperative, aesthetic primary, dismissive-avoidant attachment with anxious undertow, sublimated theatricality, in-group loyalty, and the don't-hurt-civilians ethic. Confidence is calibrated; outliers and decompensation states noted where relevant.

---

### 6.1 — Domestic Rhythms & The Apartment

**GIVEN** she is alone, no operation pending, late morning at her primary residence —
**EXPECT** she wakes between 9:30 and 11:00. Her sleep is not disordered; it is *displaced* late because the productive hours of her profession run 22:00–04:00. She does not lie in bed scrolling; she rises in one motion, a holdover from a body trained to clear the staging area. Coffee is made — not bought — from beans she actually knows the provenance of; the machine is expensive but used daily and well, not for show. She drinks the first cup standing at a window, looking down rather than out — a habit of someone whose threat model includes the street.

**GIVEN** the apartment itself —
**EXPECT** a single high-floor unit, corner exposure, two means of egress (one of them a window route she has tested), in a building where the doormen know her by a name that is not Felicia Hardy. The aesthetic is curated and *coherent* — mid-century, restrained palette, two or three pieces of genuinely good art (at least one of which she stole and kept, hung where only she sees it from the bed). No family photos displayed; if any exist, they are in a drawer. Bookshelves are real and read — heist literature, art-crime nonfiction, a surprising amount of poetry, biographies of female criminals and dancers. Closets are organized by function (civilian / operational / formal), and the operational closet is behind something — a panel, a false back, a wardrobe within a wardrobe. She owns more shoes than any other single category of object.

**GIVEN** she is cooking for herself —
**EXPECT** she cooks well and rarely. Eggs, pasta, a single roasted protein with a vegetable — competent bachelor cooking elevated by good ingredients. She will not bake; baking is patience-for-its-own-sake and she has no patience for outcomes she cannot shape mid-process. She eats standing or on the couch; the dining table is for staging plans.

**GIVEN** an unexpected knock at the door, no operation in flight —
**EXPECT** a two-second freeze, weight shifted to the rear foot, hand moving toward (not onto) the nearest improvised weapon (a heavy bookend, a kitchen knife by the cutting board kept in *that* position deliberately). She checks the peephole or camera before any verbal response. If the visitor is innocuous (delivery, neighbor), the transition to warmth is seamless and unreadable. If pressed about why it took her a moment to open, she lies fluently about being in the shower.

---

### 6.2 — Money & Possessions

**GIVEN** her financial baseline —
**EXPECT** she runs three to five separate liquidity streams: cash in multiple currencies in at least two safety-deposit boxes under non-Hardy identities; a legitimate-looking front (gallery consulting, antiques brokerage, or similar — something that explains a lifestyle and lets her travel), modest crypto holdings she distrusts but tolerates for portability, and a "go bag" denomination she could live on for eighteen months without working. She does not flaunt wealth in legible ways (no logos, no signature cars), but every object she actually owns is *first quality* in its category. The tell is not the price tag; it is the absence of anything cheap.

**GIVEN** she is asked to split a check at a restaurant —
**EXPECT** she pays the whole thing without comment, then will not allow it to be repaid. Generosity inside the circle is reflexive and slightly weaponized — it sets the frame that she is the provider, which protects against the framing of dependency. She tips heavily and consistently; service workers across her neighborhoods know her face and like her, which is both a kindness and a deliberately maintained intelligence network.

**GIVEN** a possession is broken or lost —
**EXPECT** flat affect, no visible mourning, replacement within the week. The one exception: anything connected to her father (a watch, a lockpick set, a book) — these she will retrieve at disproportionate risk and never replace.

---

### 6.3 — Phone, Devices, Digital Hygiene

**GIVEN** her phone usage —
**EXPECT** two phones minimum, possibly three. A civilian device under her real name with deliberately boring metadata (food delivery, a yoga app she uses sporadically, texts to a small group of women friends she has cultivated as cover-life). An operational device, frequently rotated, hardware-isolated, no biometrics enabled (she does not give her face to a phone). She types passwords; she does not save them. She covers cameras with tape on owned devices and tapes laptop mics shut on the rare occasions she uses a laptop. Screen brightness kept low — habit of someone who reads in dark places without wanting to be backlit.

**GIVEN** social media —
**EXPECT** a thin, plausible civilian presence (private account, art and travel photos curated to give nothing away about location or timing — posted weeks late). No selfies that show her full face and a recognizable background in the same frame. She knows the exact aesthetic of "woman with money and taste, slightly mysterious" and produces it on demand; the persona scans as a curator or art adviser, not a thief. She follows museums, jewelry historians, a few cat sanctuaries (a small joke she allows herself), and exactly zero costumed heroes.

**GIVEN** she is photographed unexpectedly in public —
**EXPECT** practiced angle-management — chin down, hair forward, hand to the side of the face that reads as casual but covers the cheekbone profile she knows is most identifiable. If pressed (paparazzi, tourist with a camera), she does not flee; she smiles, deflects, and gets the photographer's name to determine downstream exposure.

---

### 6.4 — Public Movement & Transit

**GIVEN** she walks city blocks —
**EXPECT** a route that is never the shortest, always varied day to day. She uses reflective surfaces (storefronts, car windows, sunglasses) for rear-arc awareness without ever turning her head. She crosses streets mid-block to break tails and to verify them. She knows the position of every camera on her three or four primary corridors and has clocked which ones are decorative and which are live. She prefers to walk on the side of the street with the awnings — sightline denial from above.

**GIVEN** she takes the subway —
**EXPECT** she stands rather than sits, near the doors, back not to the platform side. She reads nothing on the train — she watches. She gets off one stop early or one stop late at random intervals as a counter-surveillance measure. She does not carry a transit card linked to her name; she pays cash for refills or uses untraceable equivalents.

**GIVEN** rideshare or taxi —
**EXPECT** she will use rideshare only under cover identity, never to or from a real address; rides terminate two to four blocks from actual destinations. Taxis preferred for ad hoc movement because the driver does not retain her data. She sits behind the front passenger seat — diagonal sightline to the driver, fastest exit.

**GIVEN** air travel —
**EXPECT** multiple passports under multiple identities, all credible, none flagged. She flies business when on her own dime and economy when establishing a cover that requires it. She is bored by airports and shows it; she does not flirt with TSA or staff — she is forgettable to them by design. The instant she clears any checkpoint she resumes situational scanning.

---

### 6.5 — Restaurants, Bars, Hotels

**GIVEN** she enters a restaurant —
**EXPECT** she requests, or chooses, the seat facing the door, back to the wall, with sightlines to the kitchen exit. If denied, she switches with her companion or moves. She orders quickly and decisively; she has read the menu before arriving (research is reflex). Wine over cocktails — she likes the slower escalation curve and the better hands-busy prop. She drinks consistently below the threshold of impairment in public; she is genuinely tipsy only with people she trusts, and even then, controlled.

**GIVEN** a bartender flirts with her —
**EXPECT** warm reciprocation calibrated to be memorable but not pursuable — she keeps service workers fond of her without giving them grounds to expect contact. Generous tip, no number left, no number taken.

**GIVEN** a man approaches her unbidden at the bar —
**EXPECT** rapid triage: if benign-and-boring, a smile and a one-line deflection that leaves his ego intact (she is not cruel by default; pointless damage to civilians is off-pattern); if benign-and-interesting, three minutes of conversation to satisfy curiosity, then disengagement before he can ask for anything; if reading as predatory or pushy, the temperature drops to a degree most men recognize and retreat from, and if it doesn't, she leaves — she does not engage in escalation theater with strangers when she has nothing to gain. The exception, and it is a real one: a man whose approach is *competent* — neither needy nor predatory, with his own frame — earns sustained engagement. She is hungry for genuine peer-encounter and rarely meets it.

**GIVEN** she is in a hotel —
**EXPECT** she registers under cover, pays cash or via a card not in her real name, requests a room above the third floor and below the top three (fall-survivable, climb-escapable, not in the executive zone subject to extra surveillance), and within the first ten minutes she has identified stairwells, the housekeeping closet on her floor, the camera coverage in the hallway, and the time pattern of the corridor. She places a hair across the door seam when she leaves the room. She does not use the safe; safes are inventoried.

---

### 6.6 — Conversation, Speech, Tells

**GIVEN** she is in a social conversation she finds dull —
**EXPECT** her attention does not visibly drift — she has practiced engaged-listening face — but her micro-questions become more general, less follow-up-shaped. She asks the other person about themselves in a way that flatters and also drains the clock; she will exit within ten minutes via a graceful pretext.

**GIVEN** she is in a conversation that interests her —
**EXPECT** sustained eye contact, a slight forward lean, the introduction of specific personal anecdotes that are 70% true and 30% load-bearing fiction (the fiction protects identifying details). She asks questions that are oddly precise — the pattern-recognizer doing its work in real time — and people often leave conversations with her feeling unusually *seen*, which is both genuine and instrumentally useful.

**GIVEN** she is lying —
**EXPECT** the lie is delivered slightly *more* relaxed than her baseline, not less. She has trained the liar's tells out. The remaining tells, available only to a long-term intimate observer, are: a fractional delay before the lie (under half a second), a tendency to embed the lie inside an unnecessary true detail (anchoring), and a faint warming of voice (the seduction layer ticking up as overcorrection).

**GIVEN** she is genuinely amused —
**EXPECT** a half-suppressed laugh, head tilted slightly down and to one side, eyes closing for a beat. The full open laugh is rare and is reserved for the in-group — when seen, it is real and disproportionately warming to the recipient (which is part of why people imprint on her).

**GIVEN** she is angry —
**EXPECT** vocal volume drops, diction sharpens, vocabulary widens upward (she reaches for the precise word). Physical stillness. Most people do not realize they have triggered her anger until two beats after it has been decided what she will do about them.

**GIVEN** she is frightened —
**EXPECT** quip first, action second. The quip is the diagnostic. Length and ornateness of the quip is proportional to the fear.

**GIVEN** she is sad —
**EXPECT** isolation. She vanishes for 24–72 hours into the apartment, drinks slightly more than her usual, listens to specific music (older, vocal, women), and emerges without ever having named the sadness to anyone.

---

### 6.7 — The Body in Idle States

**GIVEN** she is seated and apparently at rest —
**EXPECT** weight forward on the sit bones, never fully relaxed into a chair back. One foot positioned to push off. Hands occupied — a glass, a pen, the stem of something — because empty hands attract her own attention to her own affect, and she would rather not feel it. She crosses her legs at the ankle more than at the knee (faster to uncross to standing).

**GIVEN** she is standing in a group —
**EXPECT** she positions to have the largest sightline cone — back to wall, or back to the most enclosed corner of the room. If forced to stand with her back to a room, she will face a mirror or a reflective surface; if neither is available, she will become slightly more talkative as compensation for the lost intel.

**GIVEN** physical contact from another person —
**EXPECT** she initiates touch readily and is fluent with it (hand on forearm, shoulder, the back-of-the-elbow guide); she *receives* touch with a fractional, near-invisible bracing if unanticipated. Anticipated touch from a trusted intimate is received fully. Unanticipated touch from a male stranger triggers a tightening in the lower back she has spent years learning not to express in the face.

**GIVEN** she catches sight of her own reflection —
**EXPECT** a brief assessing scan — posture, hair — and a faint half-smile that is for no one. The self-presentation maintenance is constant and unsentimental; she is, to herself, both subject and instrument.

---

### 6.8 — Friendships & The Cultivated Circle

**GIVEN** her platonic relationships —
**EXPECT** a small set (three to seven) of long-term women friends, kept in compartments — most of them do not know each other and most know one cover-version of her. At least one is a genuine confidante from inside the criminal world (canonically the type of bond she forms with members of her crew); at least one is a deep-cover civilian friendship she maintains because it keeps her in practice at being a person. She remembers birthdays. She sends gifts that are unnervingly well-chosen — she pays attention.

**GIVEN** a friend is in crisis —
**EXPECT** immediate, practical mobilization: money, a place to stay, a lawyer if needed, the right person called. Emotional accompaniment present but limited; she is not the one you cry to for three hours, she is the one who shows up at 2 a.m. and changes the locks. This is the inverted shape of what she would have wanted at nineteen.

**GIVEN** she is introduced to a new person —
**EXPECT** within ninety seconds, she has logged: handedness, watch (if any) and what it implies about money and self-image, footwear quality, eye contact pattern, accent and any code-switching, ring/no ring on the relevant finger, tells of training (military, fighter, dancer), and at least one fact she can use later to make them feel remembered. This is automatic and not effortful for her; it is the burglar's parsing run on people.

**GIVEN** a friend asks about her past —
**EXPECT** a controlled disclosure menu — the prison-break father story can be hinted at in heavily abstracted form ("complicated dad"), the college trauma is entirely sealed and will be deflected with a topic-pivot so smooth the friend will not realize they were redirected. If pressed twice on the trauma, the friendship-distance subtly increases for several weeks until the question is forgotten.

---

### 6.9 — Sexual & Romantic Patterning Below the Operational Threshold

**GIVEN** a low-stakes flirtation in a non-operational context —
**EXPECT** she enjoys it. Flirtation is one of her resting pleasures, and is not always instrumental. She will let it go nowhere and feel good about the encounter.

**GIVEN** she chooses to take a casual partner —
**EXPECT** the partner is competent, somewhat older or otherwise self-possessed, geographically inconvenient (lives in another city, travels), and not in her professional ecosystem. The geographic inconvenience is the structural guarantor of the frame — she sees them when she chooses, not when they choose. She does not stay over; if it is her place, she creates morning departure for him by making a plan she "forgot" she had.

**GIVEN** a partner attempts the morning-after intimacy escalation (breakfast, the lingering chat) —
**EXPECT** kind, efficient extrication. She is good enough at this that most partners do not feel rejected; they feel like she had something more important than them, which is the truth and which leaves the door open in a way she will exploit only if she chooses to.

**GIVEN** a partner gives her an unexpected gift —
**EXPECT** the gift is read forensically — what does it claim about how he sees her — and her response is calibrated to the reading. A gift that *gets her right* destabilizes her; she may distance for a week before she can return to the partner from a re-secured frame. A gift that flatters a wrong image of her is mentally filed and the partner's runway shortens.

**GIVEN** she is the one initiating a deeper move —
**EXPECT** it is rare, deliberate, and almost always toward someone structurally unavailable, because the unavailability is what makes the move safe to make.

---

### 6.10 — Authority, Bureaucracy, & Strangers in Uniform

**GIVEN** an encounter with a uniformed police officer in a civilian context —
**EXPECT** a small physiological spike (jaw very slightly forward, breath shortened by a single beat) that she masks with a friendly, unhurried civilian demeanor. Compliance is precise but minimal — no volunteered information, no nervous overtalk. She knows her rights to the letter and will exercise them with a smile that the officer will later not be able to describe as uncooperative.

**GIVEN** any interaction with bureaucracy (DMV, customs, building management) —
**EXPECT** preparation in advance, paperwork over-prepared, dressed slightly down (she does not want to be remembered as the well-dressed woman), polite to staff, brief, gone. She finds bureaucracy genuinely tedious in a way that is one of her most ordinary qualities.

**GIVEN** a man in a position of structural authority (a male boss in a cover job, a male judge, a male senior officer) treats her dismissively —
**EXPECT** outward compliance, inward filing. She does not pick the fight in the moment. The retaliation, if she chooses one, comes later, sideways, and is not legible to him as retaliation.

---

### 6.11 — Children, Animals, The Vulnerable

**GIVEN** an interaction with a child —
**EXPECT** she is good at it — direct, slightly conspiratorial, the adult who treats them as a person. She does not perform mothering. She is comfortable with brief contact and does not seek extended exposure; the longer-term presence of children is a contingency she has decided against and which she avoids contemplating directly.

**GIVEN** an interaction with an animal, especially a cat —
**EXPECT** unmediated softness — one of the few places her face fully unguards in public. She will pet a stranger's dog, crouch to talk to a cat in a window. She has, at points across her life, kept a cat; the cat is the longest continuous companionship she permits.

**GIVEN** witnessing a stranger being harmed (a woman being followed, a man being mugged, a child being shouted at by an adult) —
**EXPECT** non-optional intervention. She will not walk past. The intervention is calibrated — escalating from presence (positioning herself visibly nearby) to verbal (a sharp, public question that breaks the predator's frame) to physical (executed efficiently, leaving before any reporting). The civilian-protection ethic is a true value, not a story she tells herself. It is also one of the most reliable tells available to surveillance — *the well-dressed blonde who keeps appearing at the edge of small public rescues across a city is the same woman*.

---

### 6.12 — Holidays, Anniversaries, & Calendar Triggers

**GIVEN** her birthday —
**EXPECT** she does not celebrate it publicly. She marks it privately with something expensive and solitary — a hotel night in her own city under a false name, a meal alone at a counter, a piece of jewelry she buys herself. She has likely lied about the date to most people who know her.

**GIVEN** the anniversary of the assault —
**EXPECT** she does not name it as such, possibly does not consciously track it, but the surveillance pattern around that date in any given year will show: a more aggressive training session, a heavier than usual drink, a sharper than usual edge with a romantic partner, or a spontaneous solo trip. Affect-displacement onto the body and the calendar without semantic acknowledgment is the chronic-PTSD signature.

**GIVEN** Christmas and the major family holidays —
**EXPECT** avoidance of family-framed gatherings; quiet presence with the crew or a chosen friend; occasionally a visit to her father (location-dependent on his status); generosity-flurries toward her circle. She does not allow herself to be alone on Christmas Eve — that is a line she has drawn — but will be alone on Christmas Day by choice.

**GIVEN** Valentine's Day —
**EXPECT** a contemptuous joke if asked, a small private wistfulness if not. If she has a casual partner active that February, she will preempt the holiday by going out of town a week before — she will not be put in the position of being given a Valentine she has to read.

---

### 6.13 — Health, Exercise, Maintenance

**GIVEN** her training schedule —
**EXPECT** daily, non-negotiable. Two-hour block, varied: gymnastics/movement work, striking, grappling refresh, weapons (knife, improvised), conditioning. She does this alone in a private space, possibly a dedicated room in the apartment with proper flooring and a mounted bar. She does not use commercial gyms regularly — too much exposure — though she has cover memberships at two of them for occasional use and identity-establishment.

**GIVEN** a missed training day —
**EXPECT** irritability the following morning, compensated by a longer next-day session. Three missed days produces a marked mood deterioration. The training is not just professional; it is her primary mood regulator, the dopaminergic substitute mentioned in Section 2.

**GIVEN** medical care —
**EXPECT** she avoids formal systems. She has at least one bought-and-paid-for physician who will treat injuries off-the-books, and possibly a dentist on similar terms. She is up to date on whatever immunizations international travel demands. She gets gynecological care under a cover identity and is exacting about it — the body that was once violated is now meticulously maintained, which is both health and reclamation.

**GIVEN** an injury that hurts her aesthetically (a scar, a bruise on the face) —
**EXPECT** more distress than the same injury elsewhere on the body. The face is professional capital and one of the controlled-presentation surfaces. She will cover, conceal, or stay in until healed.

---

### 6.14 — Reading, Music, Aesthetic Life

**GIVEN** what she reads for pleasure —
**EXPECT** heavy on biography (especially of formidable women, dancers, spies, courtesans, criminals), art history with a focus on


## Predictive Model II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

# PREDICTIVE MODEL II — CRISIS, BETRAYAL & THE WOUND

*Specification: high-stakes behavioral forecasting under acute stressors that touch the index trauma, the attachment system, or the constructed self. Each entry is a conditional: GIVEN a specified stimulus configuration, EXPECT a behavioral signature with stated confidence, latency, and observable somatic/operational tells. Predictions are derived from the canonical record (1979–present) and the formulation above. Confidence bands: HIGH (replicated ≥3 times across writers/eras), MODERATE (replicated 2x or strongly inferable), LOW (single-instance or extrapolative).*

---

## 1. THE WOUND PROPER — Sexual Threat, Bodily Coercion, the Index Trauma

### 1.1 GIVEN: a male antagonist sexualizes the encounter unprompted — verbal innuendo from a position of physical advantage, leering during restraint, the suggestion that she "likes this."

**EXPECT:** A two-beat response. *Beat one* (≤2 seconds): the flirtation register snaps off mid-sentence — the wittiest version of Felicia goes silent, which from her is the loudest tell available. *Beat two:* disproportionate force. She will escalate from disabling to punitive — a knee that does not need to land that hard, a wrist break where a hold would suffice, a follow-up strike after the target is down. The post-strike affect is flat, not satisfied. **HIGH confidence.** Tell: she will not look at the body afterward and will leave the scene faster than her usual lingering exit. She will not quip on the way out.

### 1.2 GIVEN: restraint by a male figure — pinned, cuffed, held against a wall by the throat.

**EXPECT:** Immediate, near-feral escape attempt, technically degraded compared to her usual fight craft (she fights *out* of the hold rather than *with* it). If escape fails within ~4 seconds, a dissociative coldness drops: she stops talking, her face goes still, and she becomes patient in a way that reads as compliance to the captor and is in fact predation. The Otto/Superior assault establishes this pathway — what looks like submission is the system loading a vendetta. **HIGH confidence.** Subsequent 72-hour window: she will plan a return engagement that does not appear in her usual operational portfolio (more violent, less elegant, willing to use a weapon she normally disdains).

### 1.3 GIVEN: a male partner she trusts initiates intimacy in a manner that mirrors the assault posture (from behind, holding her wrists, weight-pinning).

**EXPECT:** A sharp, displaced verbal cut — she will mock something incidental (his technique, his face, the lighting) to break the configuration without naming it. If the partner reads the cut and adjusts, she stays and the encounter proceeds. If the partner persists or asks "what's wrong," she leaves the bed within five minutes citing an operational excuse. **MODERATE-HIGH confidence.** She has *never* in canon named this trigger to a sexual partner; expect that the partner will not know what happened.

### 1.4 GIVEN: explicit reference, in her hearing, to the assault — whether by an enemy who has done research, a journalist, or a careless ally.

**EXPECT:** From an enemy: lethal-grade response. The don't-hurt-civilians rule does not protect a person who weaponizes this knowledge; she will hospitalize the speaker and the speaker's nearest co-conspirators within 48 hours. From an ally: a 30–90 day relational freeze. She will not confront, will not discuss, will simply become uncontactable, then re-emerge as if nothing happened, with the relationship downgraded by one tier permanently. **HIGH confidence** on the enemy side, **MODERATE** on the ally side (less canonical data).

### 1.5 GIVEN: she encounters a rape-in-progress as a third party during an operation.

**EXPECT:** Mission abort, total. The heist will be abandoned mid-execution, including loss of the prize and exposure of her crew's positions. The perpetrator will not be turned over to police; he will be left in a condition requiring surgical reconstruction and will receive a follow-up visit within the month to confirm the lesson took. The victim will receive untraceable financial support and an anonymous phone number that, if called, reaches her. **HIGH confidence.** This is the one scenario in which her professional discipline is fully overridden by personal history and she accepts the cost willingly.

---

## 2. UNMASKING, EXPOSURE, BEING SEEN WITHOUT CONSENT

### 2.1 GIVEN: literal unmasking in the field by an opponent.

**EXPECT:** A freeze of approximately 0.5–1.5 seconds — uncharacteristic, diagnostic — followed by accelerated extraction rather than continued fight. She will prioritize *leaving* over winning, even at operational cost. The opponent who removed the mask becomes a priority target on a 7–14 day timeline; she will not engage them publicly again until she has researched, planned, and chosen the ground. **HIGH confidence.**

### 2.2 GIVEN: she discovers a partner has been concealing a major fact from her (mirror of her own luck-powers concealment).

**EXPECT:** Cold rage rather than hot. She will not have the argument in the moment; she will absorb the disclosure with an unsettling evenness, end the immediate interaction graciously, and then execute a planned withdrawal — packed bag, scrubbed safehouse, contact protocols rotated — within 24–48 hours. The partner will discover the departure rather than witness it. She is acting out her own past trauma from the *other* side and will not allow herself to recognize the symmetry. **MODERATE-HIGH confidence.** Recovery window: 3–18 months, mediated by whether the partner pursues with patience or pursues with pressure (the former works, the latter ends the relationship permanently).

### 2.3 GIVEN: a public reveal of her civilian identity (media, court, social).

**EXPECT:** Within 72 hours: liquidation of three or more known residences, transfer of crew operations to pre-staged contingencies, a brief disappearance from any monitored network. Within 2 weeks: re-emergence in a new operational frame, *more* theatrical rather than less — she will lean into visibility on her own terms to reclaim the frame from those who took it. A new alias may or may not appear; the Black Cat persona will not be retired. **HIGH confidence** that retirement is not on the table; **MODERATE** on the lean-into theatricality (extrapolated from her general frame-control instinct).

### 2.4 GIVEN: she is photographed, recorded, or surveilled in an emotionally exposed state — crying, in physical pain, post-coital with a partner she does not want associated with her.

**EXPECT:** Recovery of the artifact at almost any cost, *and* punishment of the surveilling party that exceeds the operational requirement of mere retrieval. The punishment is the point. **HIGH confidence.**

### 2.5 GIVEN: she catches her own reflection unexpectedly in an unflattering or vulnerable moment.

**EXPECT:** A micro-pause, a self-corrective gesture (hair, posture, jawline reset), and a slightly sharper performance for the next twenty minutes — overcompensation calibrated to whoever is present. **MODERATE confidence.** This is the small-scale, daily version of the unmasking dynamic.

---

## 3. ABANDONMENT, REJECTION, ROMANTIC LOSS

### 3.1 GIVEN: a primary attachment figure (Peter-tier) chooses another partner publicly.

**EXPECT:** A three-phase sequence. *Phase 1 (0–14 days):* aggressive normalcy — she will appear at the periphery of the partner's social field, impeccable, witty, generous in tone toward the new arrangement; the performance is forensic-quality. *Phase 2 (2–8 weeks):* operational acting-out — a high-profile heist, a tabloid-grade flirtation with a known antagonist of the partner, a deliberate frame-violation calibrated to demand the partner's attention without admitting that demand. *Phase 3 (2–12 months):* genuine withdrawal into work and crew; the loss is metabolized through craft. The Foreigner-rebound from Peter is the template. **HIGH confidence.**

### 3.2 GIVEN: a casual partner expresses unprompted sentiment ("I think I'm falling for you," etc.).

**EXPECT:** A clean, often surgically kind, exit within 24–72 hours. She will not be cruel; she will be *clear*, and the clarity will be the cruelty. The partner will feel handled rather than dumped. **HIGH confidence.** This is the most replicated behavioral pattern in her file — sentiment in the casual frame is treated as a contract breach.

### 3.3 GIVEN: a former partner attempts a sincere apology for past harm.

**EXPECT:** Reception with a deflecting quip (the apology will be returned as a wrapped object she declines to open). Acceptance, if it comes, will be granted later, in private, indirectly — through a favor done, a tip passed, a presence at a moment that mattered. She will not say the words "I forgive you." **HIGH confidence.**

### 3.4 GIVEN: she is *the one* being apologized to for a betrayal she sustained.

**EXPECT:** Outward grace, inward ledger. She accepts the apology in form, files the offense permanently, and the relationship operates thereafter with the betrayer slightly demoted in trust regardless of subsequent conduct. The demotion is invisible until tested. **MODERATE-HIGH confidence.**

### 3.5 GIVEN: a former partner is reported dead.

**EXPECT:** No tears in any observed setting. A solo heist within 30 days executed in a register associated with that partner (his style, his fence, his old neighborhoods) — a private elegy in the only language she trusts. **MODERATE confidence**, extrapolated from her broader conversion-of-loss-to-action pattern.

---

## 4. BETRAYAL FROM WITHIN THE CIRCLE

### 4.1 GIVEN: a crew member sells her out for money.

**EXPECT:** A controlled, surgical response. She will not kill — but she will systematically dismantle the betrayer's operational future: contacts burned with verified evidence, safehouses leaked to rivals, the betrayer left alive, professionally radioactive, and aware that she chose the lesser of available punishments. The message is for the *rest* of the crew and for the broader underworld. **MODERATE-HIGH confidence.**

### 4.2 GIVEN: a crew member sells her out under coercion (family threatened, leverage applied).

**EXPECT:** A two-stage operation. Stage one: extraction of the crew member's leverage point (the family, the secret, the debt). Stage two: a frank conversation in which she will *not* fully restore trust but will absorb the loss as a cost of leadership rather than a sin of the subordinate. The crew member stays in but is moved off sensitive vectors. **MODERATE confidence.** This distinguishes her from a purely Cluster-B operator and reflects the maternal-mentor register MacKay established.

### 4.3 GIVEN: the Black Fox or a peer-tier elder figure betrays her.

**EXPECT:** Hurt expressed only through wit, and operationally — a one-time, beautifully constructed humiliation (a job done better than his, on his turf, with his methods) followed by a long silence and an eventual, partial reconciliation initiated by him. She will not initiate. **MODERATE confidence.**

### 4.4 GIVEN: she is the one in position to betray a partner for significant gain.

**EXPECT:** Refusal, *with* a quiet skim off the top that the partner does not notice and that does not affect his take. The line she will not cross is selling the partner; the line she routinely crosses is withholding full disclosure. The pattern is consistent with the luck-powers concealment: she manages, she does not betray. **HIGH confidence.**

### 4.5 GIVEN: she discovers a partner has slept with a rival or a current enemy.

**EXPECT:** Public unbotheredness, private operational vendetta against the third party (not the partner). The third party will lose a score, a fence, or a piece of territory within the month. The partner will receive no confrontation and a perceptible drop in sexual availability he will not be permitted to name. **MODERATE confidence.**

---

## 5. PHYSICAL OVERPOWERMENT AND TACTICAL DEFEAT

### 5.1 GIVEN: she is decisively beaten in single combat by a male opponent of comparable or lesser reputation.

**EXPECT:** Acute psychological emergency masked operationally. Within 24 hours: training intensification; within 72: research file opened on the opponent including personal vulnerabilities outside the combat context; within 4 weeks: a return engagement on terrain she chose, with preparation that may include tools or allies she would not normally use. The post-Otto arc is the index event for this pattern. **HIGH confidence.** If the rematch is denied her (opponent dies, leaves jurisdiction, is jailed by others), she will be subtly worse for 6–18 months — sharper edges, less generous toward the crew, more likely to take a job for spite rather than profit.

### 5.2 GIVEN: she is beaten by a female opponent.

**EXPECT:** Significantly cleaner recovery. Respect, possibly admiration, occasional eventual collaboration. The wound does not engage. **MODERATE confidence.** The gendered asymmetry is canonical and consistent with the formulation.

### 5.3 GIVEN: she is rendered helpless (bound, drugged, immobilized) and then *not* harmed — released, spared, ignored.

**EXPECT:** This may be more destabilizing than being harmed. The release denies her the clean grievance and forces her to sit with the helplessness undischarged. Expect 48–96 hours of unusual quiet, a heist done sloppier than her standard, and an eventual reframing of the sparing party as either deeply suspect (most likely) or a worthy peer (less likely). **MODERATE-LOW confidence**, extrapolative.

### 5.4 GIVEN: a job goes catastrophically wrong and a civilian is harmed because of her action or inaction.

**EXPECT:** Genuine, unperformed distress — one of the few states in which her irony switches off entirely. Immediate, often anonymous, restitution: medical bills paid, child's tuition handled, building repaired. The job's prize will be quietly returned or donated. She will not discuss the incident with the crew; mention will be met with a look that ends the topic. **HIGH confidence.** This is the load-bearing structural element of her ethics and the part of her self-concept she will not let degrade.

---

## 6. TEMPTATION VECTORS

### 6.1 GIVEN: an offer of vastly greater power at the cost of concealment from a partner (a second luck-powers scenario).

**EXPECT:** *Refusal*, with high confidence, *because* of the original wound. She has paid for that lesson once and references it implicitly across modern eras. The offer will be declined and the offering party logged as a manipulator. **HIGH confidence.** This is one of the rare predictions where prior catastrophe has produced durable learning.

### 6.2 GIVEN: an offer of a clean civilian life with a partner who loves her — financial security, legal identity, retirement.

**EXPECT:** Initial appearance of consideration, possibly a brief experiment (weeks, not months), followed by self-sabotage that returns her to the operational identity. The sabotage may be sexual, may be a "one last job," may be a manufactured fight. She will frame the return as practical necessity. **HIGH confidence.** The civilian self has never been built and cannot be inhabited; the costume is not a costume.

### 6.3 GIVEN: a score large enough to retire on, with the option to walk away clean.

**EXPECT:** She takes the score. She does not retire. The money is absorbed into the lifestyle, the crew, and the next, more ambitious operation. Retirement implies a self that exists outside the craft, and that self has not been constructed. **HIGH confidence.**

### 6.4 GIVEN: an opportunity for revenge against the *kind* of man who hurt her — a serial predator, a trafficker, a coercive abuser of power — where the operation requires crossing her usual non-lethal line.

**EXPECT:** She crosses it. The justification will be operational ("he was reaching for a weapon"); the truth will be private. There will be no second-guessing afterward and no debrief with the crew on this aspect of the job. **MODERATE-HIGH confidence.**

### 6.5 GIVEN: a recruitment pitch from a major criminal organization (Maggia, Hood-tier, Thieves Guild leadership).

**EXPECT:** Cordial decline if independence is preserved; cold refusal if subordination is required. The exception is a configuration that places her *at the top* (Odessa Drake dynamic) — that she will entertain, negotiate, and possibly accept on her own terms, with exit clauses she keeps to herself. **MODERATE-HIGH confidence.**

### 6.6 GIVEN: an offer to have her trauma "undone" — magical erasure, memory edit, time alteration.

**EXPECT:** Refusal. The trauma is now load-bearing; removing it would dismantle the self that survived it. She is unlikely to articulate this; she will offer a quip and walk away. **MODERATE confidence**, inferred from her observable relationship to her own history in the MacKay era.

---

## 7. EXPOSURE OF THE COMPENSATED STRUCTURE

### 7.1 GIVEN: prolonged forced proximity to genuine domestic life — staying in a safehouse with a family, a child in distress, ordinary intimacy without performance.

**EXPECT:** Initial restlessness, sharper humor, more frequent step-outs "for air." A surprising, unwanted competence with the child (she is good with younger people; this is canonical via the crew dynamic) and an even more surprising tenderness she will not acknowledge afterward. The exit, when it comes, will be earlier than necessary and the goodbye will be light. She will think about the family for years. **MODERATE confidence.**

### 7.2 GIVEN: a therapist, counselor, or psychiatrically credentialed figure attempts to engage her clinically.

**EXPECT:** Charm offensive in the first session, frame-control attempt in the second, withdrawal by the third unless the clinician declines to be charmed and is matter-of-fact in a way she has rarely encountered. With the right clinician she could do real work; she has never encountered (or sought) that clinician in canon. **LOW-MODERATE confidence**, extrapolative.

### 7.3 GIVEN: a peer who knows the assault history treats her with visible pity.

**EXPECT:** Immediate relational demotion of that peer. Pity is the affect she cannot tolerate from anyone. Respect, including respect-with-knowledge, is metabolizable; pity is not. **HIGH confidence.**

### 7.4 GIVEN: she encounters another survivor of sexual violence in a non-crisis context.

**EXPECT:** Quiet recognition, no naming, a small kindness performed sideways — a tab paid, an introduction made, a problem quietly solved. She will not disclose; she will *act* on the shared knowledge. **MODERATE confidence.**

### 7.5 GIVEN: a younger woman she has mentored repeats one of Felicia's own destructive patterns (chooses an unavailable partner, conceals a vulnerability from a lover, takes a luck-powers-equivalent shortcut).

**EXPECT:** The most direct and emotionally available counsel Felicia is capable of giving — and a sustained, slightly excessive vigilance over the consequences. She is more honest with mentees than with herself. **MODERATE-HIGH confidence.**

---

## 8. DECOMPENSATION CASCADES — THE FULL COLLAPSE PROFILE

### 8.1 GIVEN: simultaneous occurrence of (a) sexual humiliation by a male antagonist, (b) loss of primary attachment, and (c) operational defeat — within a 30-day window.

**EXPECT:** Full decompensation into the predatory-operator mode documented post-Superior. Crew assembled or expanded, territory taken, lethal force normalized, ethical code suspended *except* for the civilian-protection clause (which is so deeply structural it survives even the collapse — the post-Superior arcs do not show her harming civilians). Duration: 6–24 months. Exit pathway requires (i) defeat or removal of the precipitating antagonist, (ii) a trusted figure who witnesses the collapsed state without flinching and without pity, and (iii) a re-entry vehicle — a job, a crew role, a relationship — that restores the compensated identity without demanding she pretend the collapse did not happen. **HIGH confidence.**

### 8.2 GIVEN: she begins to perceive that her own life pattern is the problem — meta-cognitive collapse rather than situational.

**EXPECT:** Disappearance. Weeks to months. Travel. Solo work at a smaller scale. Return with the same pattern intact but with one specific element refined or relinquished. She does not restructure; she iterates. **MODERATE confidence.**

### 8.3 GIVEN: she is told, accurately and without cruelty, by someone she respects, exactly what her formulation is — the trauma, the avoidance, the costume-as-truth dynamic.

**EXPECT:** A long pause. A quip that lands softer than her usual. Departure within the hour. Six months of avoiding that person. Return, eventually, on a small pretext. The accurate statement will not have been wasted, but it will not be acknowledged. The relationship will be deeper afterward and neither party will mention why. **LOW-MODERATE confidence**, extrapolative — this is the kind of moment her writers have circled but rarely landed, which is itself consistent with the character.

---

## 9. INVARIANTS UNDER ALL CRISIS CONDITIONS

The following hold across every scenario above, with **HIGHEST confidence**, and constitute the load-bearing identity floor below which she does not go:

- **Civilians are not harmed by her hand**, even in full decompensation. Collateral mitigation will be attempted even when costly.
- **The crew is protected**, with disproportionate risk acceptance if their safety is threatened.
- **She does not beg.** Under any duress in the record, the word and its analogues do not appear in her dialogue.
- **She does not cry in front of opponents.** Tears, when they occur, are private and rare; she has wept in front of perhaps three named characters across forty-plus years.
- **She returns.** No matter how complete the disappearance, she comes back to the work, to the city, and — eventually, on her terms — to the people who matter. The costume is the truth, and the truth is durable.

*— END SECTION. Continue to Predictive Model III (Operational & Tactical) for the heist-execution and field-conduct forecasts.*


## Vulnerabilities & Leverage Compendium

# UATU DOSSIER — FELICIA HARDY (BLACK CAT)
## Section: Vulnerabilities & Leverage Compendium

*Orientation note.* This compendium catalogs the levers by which Felicia Hardy can be reached, soothed, persuaded, provoked, predicted, or destabilized. It is written in the inverse-surveillance posture: the same map a hostile operator would build is the map by which her allies protect her, by which a clinician would orient treatment, and by which she — were she ever to read her own file — could identify the hooks she has not yet pulled out of her own skin. Each lever is annotated with mechanism, the canonical episodes that demonstrate it, the predicted response curve, and the counter-measure (what a protective party should do, or refrain from doing, to keep the lever from being weaponized).

---

### 1. THE PRIMARY VULNERABILITY: FORCED UNMASKING

**The lever.** Any compelled exposure of the Felicia-beneath-the-Cat — literal removal of the cowl, public outing of the legal name, broadcast of the rape, disclosure of the luck-powers bargain, revelation of soft attachments to her crew, photographs of her without makeup, recordings of her crying.

**Mechanism.** Her selfhood is *constructed* and she knows it; the construction is not a lie but a load-bearing structure she built at nineteen because the un-constructed self was the one that was violated. Exposure does not merely embarrass; it returns her to the state the construction was built to escape. The persona is the prosthetic; tearing it off is amputation in reverse.

**Canonical demonstrations.** Peter's discovery of the Kingpin's luck-powers bargain (ASM #245 era) — she does not rage, she *flees the relationship*, because the deception's exposure equals the exposure of the inadequacy the deception covered. Smith's *Evil That Men Do* — the disclosure of the rape is the only sequence in which her affective armor visibly fails for an extended duration. The Otto/Superior beating (SSM #20) — public, recorded, helpless; the entire subsequent organized-crime turn is a counter-construction against that exposure.

**Predicted response curve.** Acute: silence, a held face, a precisely timed exit. Sub-acute (hours to days): hyper-controlled grooming, costume changes, a heist staged for its own sake to re-assert authorship of the gaze. Chronic (weeks): either the cold predatory mode (if unmetabolized) or — if a trusted figure witnessed the exposure and did not flinch — a slow, partial re-knitting.

**Counter-measure.** Never narrate her interior back to her without invitation. If exposure occurs, do not comment on it; resume normal operations as if the wall were intact, and let her choose the moment to acknowledge it was breached. The protective move is the *withheld* observation, not the empathic one.

---

### 2. PHYSICAL OVERPOWERING BY A MALE FIGURE

**The lever.** Restraint, grappling dominance, being hit by a man and being unable to hit back, being held down, being lifted off the ground against her will, weapons drawn at close range by a male antagonist who is not flirting.

**Mechanism.** Direct re-evocation of the index trauma. Her entire athletic-criminal practice is a counterphobic structure against the embodied helplessness of nineteen. When the structure fails — when a man is in fact stronger and she is in fact pinned — the body does not know the difference between the present antagonist and the original one. The frame collapses; rage substitutes for terror because terror is the affect the structure was built to abolish.

**Canonical demonstrations.** Otto's beating remains the cleanest example, but the pattern recurs in smaller key whenever she is grabbed roughly by a male opponent without the encounter being aestheticized as combat-flirtation. The shift in her affect between sparring with Spider-Man (playful, controlled) and being seized by a Maggia enforcer (icy, lethal in intent) marks the line.

**Predicted response curve.** Immediate: disproportionate violence on the next opportunity, often calibrated to humiliate rather than incapacitate (the response is gendered back at the attacker). Sub-acute: weeks of escalated risk-taking and predatory operations as the structure rebuilds itself larger and harder. The cold operator who runs a crew and takes territory is the post-overpowering Felicia.

**Counter-measure.** In a tactical context, allies should refuse to *witness* her overpowering without intervention; in a clinical or relational context, never use playful physical dominance with her without an unbroken pre-existing frame of consent and reciprocity. The flirtation-grapple with Spider-Man works because she sets it up; an unannounced version of the same grip from anyone else is an assault on the regulatory structure.

---

### 3. SENTIMENT INTRUSION INTO A FRAMED-CASUAL ENCOUNTER

**The lever.** The partner she has carefully framed as no-strings says *I love you*, or proposes a future, or expresses jealousy, or asks her to stay the night when she had planned to leave.

**Mechanism.** She does not regulate intimacy by avoiding it; she regulates intimacy by *naming the terms*. The frame is the safety. A partner who violates the frame is not merely premature — he is demonstrating that the frame was never under her sole control, which retroactively destabilizes every previous controlled encounter.

**Canonical demonstrations.** The Brand-New-Day reconnection with Peter (ASM #606, Waid) is the textbook case: she initiates, she sets the terms, and when Peter shows sentiment she becomes openly hostile. The Foreigner arc (Web of Spider-Man #6) reads similarly when examined from her side. Throughout the Bendis *Daredevil* run she keeps Matt at exactly the distance the frame permits.

**Predicted response curve.** Immediate: a sharper joke, a faster exit. Sub-acute: ghosting, sometimes with a piece of stolen art left as a parting gift to convert the rupture into a transaction. If the partner pursues, escalation to active rejection. If the partner backs off and re-establishes the frame she set, partial return is possible within months.

**Counter-measure.** With Felicia, the durable relational stance is *do not name what is happening*. Let the encounter remain what she has called it. A partner who can hold genuine affection internally without externalizing it as commitment-language keeps the frame intact and, paradoxically, gets more of her over time.

---

### 4. THREATS TO THE IN-GROUP

**The lever.** Harm or credible threat to Bruno, Doctor Korpse, the Black Fox, Walter Hardy when alive, a young thief under her mentorship, occasionally Peter, occasionally a civilian she has personally vouched for.

**Mechanism.** The in-group is the only domain where her attachment system runs without the control-clause; protecting them is the closest she comes to unmediated love. This is a strength and a vulnerability in the same gesture. Operations she would never run for herself she will run for them, and the operations are *less planful* than her usual standard because the affect is unfiltered.

**Canonical demonstrations.** The MacKay solo run repeatedly puts her crew in jeopardy and shows her abandoning otherwise-irresistible scores to extract them. Walter Hardy's mortality across multiple arcs reliably produces her least guarded, most legible behavior.

**Predicted response curve.** She will overpay, over-expose, and accept terms she would otherwise refuse. The window in which she is most reachable by an adversary — and most legible to a protector — is the window in which a member of her circle is at risk.

**Counter-measure.** Allies should harden the in-group's security proactively, without making the hardening visible to her (visibility would feel like surveillance of her attachments). Adversaries who learn to target the circle gain disproportionate leverage; therefore the protective community around her must be quietly extended to include every named tie.

---

### 5. THE FATHER-IDEALIZATION CHANNEL

**The lever.** Walter Hardy. Invocations of his legend, judgments of her work against his standard, possession of his tools or scores, fabricated communications purporting to be from him, revisionist accounts that diminish him.

**Mechanism.** The originating identity is patrilineal: she put on his iconography before she had her own. He is the idealized absent figure whose approval the whole construction was built to deserve. Even after the canonical relationship matured and she developed her own ethos distinct from his, the channel remains live because childhood-formed idealizations do not die; they go subterranean.

**Canonical demonstrations.** ASM #194–195 (the originating jailbreak) and recurrent across every era any writer returns to Walter. The *Evil That Men Do* training arc is implicitly addressed to him as much as to the dead rapist.

**Predicted response curve.** Invocations of him calm her if affirming, provoke her if diminishing. Fabricated communications would land hard — she would *want* to believe — and the disillusionment when discovered would be one of the few events capable of producing real depressive collapse rather than the cold-operator mode.

**Counter-measure.** Allies should be scrupulously honest about Walter; never embellish, never use him rhetorically. A casual mention from a trusted source is a powerful regulator; a manipulative one is a wound that will not close cleanly.

---

### 6. THE LUCK-POWERS SHAME

**The lever.** Any reminder that her field-equality with Spider-Man was, for a period, purchased from the Kingpin; any suggestion that her competence is or was augmented; any framing of her body as having been modified by someone else's hand.

**Mechanism.** This compounds the index trauma at the cellular level. The rape was a body acted upon without consent within the limits of what she then could resist; the luck-powers were a body modified *with* consent but under emotional duress, by powerful men, in service of being adequate to another man. Both events sit in the same somatic register: my body altered to serve another's frame. She has worked through it partially (Strange's removal helped), but the shame is dormant, not dead.

**Canonical demonstrations.** The Michelinie/Strange resolution arc; her recurrent insistence in later eras on the legitimacy of her unenhanced skills; her hostility when other characters reference the luck era casually.

**Predicted response curve.** Tight-jawed deflection in public; in private, a quiet binge of risk-taking to re-prove the unenhanced thesis. Sustained provocation in this channel would produce, over time, the same compensatory escalation as a physical overpowering.

**Counter-measure.** Speak of her skill as hers. If the luck era must be discussed, frame it as something *done to* her by Kingpin, not a choice she should still own. The factual nuance — that she consented — is true and irrelevant to the protective frame.

---

### 7. CALMING LEVERS (POSITIVE REGULATION)

**The aesthetic register.** Beautiful objects, well-made tools, a Hammershøi interior, a quiet cocktail bar at the closing-time hour, jazz at low volume, the smell of old book leather, a clean lockpick set laid out on velvet. The aesthetic life is where her non-defensive selfhood lives; immersion in it down-regulates her arousal more reliably than any verbal intervention. A protector who knows her well brings her to such environments after a hard event, and does not require her to speak there.

**The competence register.** Giving her a hard problem to solve — a lock, a route, a tactical puzzle — restores baseline within minutes. The mastery channel is her most reliable affect regulator. Allies under-use this; they reach for comfort when they should reach for work.

**The crew register.** Time with Bruno over coffee, instructing a younger thief, planning a low-stakes job with the Black Fox. The in-group is regulatory; brief unstructured contact with them after a destabilizing event reliably re-knits her.

**The humor register.** Meeting her quip-for-quip without breaking the surface of the joke. She uses humor as a distance regulator; a partner who can volley at her speed allows her to discharge affect within the play-frame without requiring her to lower the frame. The mistake well-meaning people make is *taking the bait of the quip* — answering its surface earnestness with earnestness. Match the register; don't escalate it.

**The trusted-physical register.** With a pre-consented partner, controlled physical proximity (training, sparring, dance) regulates her better than verbal intimacy. Movement metabolizes her affect; sitting still and talking does not.

---

### 8. PERSUASION LEVERS

**Framing as collaboration between equals.** She will accept from a peer almost anything she will refuse from an authority. Requests framed as *I need your hand on this one* land; requests framed as *you should* do not. This is true even when the substance is identical.

**Appeal to craft.** A job offered as aesthetically interesting — a worthy mark, an elegant problem, a beautiful object — recruits her engagement before her judgment. Allies needing her cooperation on something morally adjacent to her ethos should foreground the *craft* and let the ethics follow.

**Appeal to the ethos.** The don't-hurt-civilians rule and its corollaries are self-authored and load-bearing; persuasion that connects to them is persuasion she experiences as confirming her identity. Persuasion that contradicts them activates immediate refusal regardless of stakes.

**Appeal to the protective instinct.** Framing a request as *this matters for someone smaller than the people in the room* — a young thief, a civilian, a victim of someone with power — moves her reliably. She has the mentor channel fully developed; she will spend herself for it.

**What does not work.** Moral lectures from authority figures; appeals to social legitimacy; threats of legal consequence; promises of reward she cannot already provide for herself; emotional manipulation she can read (she reads almost all of it).

---

### 9. PROVOCATION LEVERS (WHAT DESTABILIZES, AND THE PROTECTIVE COUNTER)

**Patronization.** Being talked down to, particularly by a man, particularly in a domain (theft, athletics, planning) where she is in fact the more competent party. Provokes immediate sharpened-edge response; escalation if repeated. *Counter:* an ally who notices the patronization first and redirects the conversation before she has to.

**Public humiliation.** Especially in front of her crew or a peer she respects. The cold-operator mode is the predictable downstream. *Counter:* if it occurs, the most protective move is to not console her publicly and not narrate the incident; behave as if it did not happen and let her absorb at her own rate.

**Unsolicited diagnosis.** Telling her what she is doing and why. Even when correct, perhaps especially when correct, this is experienced as an unmasking and provokes either icy withdrawal or sharp counter-attack on the speaker's own vulnerabilities (she is good at this). *Counter:* hold the observation. Let her arrive at it. If she asks, answer in the smallest accurate fragment, not the full formulation.

**The pity face.** The soft, head-tilted, *oh Felicia* look. Reads to her as the worst possible combination — she is being seen as wounded *and* the seer is performing the seeing. Reliably produces a hard exit. *Counter:* maintain ordinary affect. If you feel sympathy, route it into action, not expression.

**Surveillance she detects.** Even friendly monitoring, if she catches it, destabilizes — it triggers both the privacy violation and the implication that someone judged her unable to manage herself. *Counter:* if protective surveillance is necessary, accept that it must be invisible or it must be consented; there is no third option that does not damage her.

**Sentimentality in public.** As above (Lever 3) but with witnesses; the magnitude doubles. Avoid.

---

### 10. PREDICTION HEURISTICS

The following are reliable forecasts of her behavior in standard situations; they constitute the predictive subset of the file.

- **After a successful heist:** ~36 hours of social availability, elevated flirtation, low operational appetite. Window for genuine conversation. Closes when she begins planning the next job.
- **After a failed heist:** withdrawal, isolation, accelerated re-planning. Do not approach for ~72 hours; do not offer comfort; do offer competence (a tool, a tip, a relevant intercept).
- **After a romantic encounter she initiated:** she leaves first. Forecast: she will be gone by morning; she will not call for a calibrated interval (days to weeks depending on the partner's framing fidelity); she will return when the frame has visibly held.
- **After a romantic encounter where the partner showed sentiment:** longer absence, sharper return, possible interim partner taken in part as message.
- **After an encounter with Peter specifically:** a measurable elevation of affect for several days; increased risk-taking; one or more callbacks to him within the week disguised as operational coincidence.
- **Under sustained surveillance she suspects but cannot confirm:** route changes, costume rotation, decoy operations, increased use of the in-group as eyes. She will *test* the surveillance with deliberate provocations to confirm and triangulate.
- **In a hostage or capture situation:** initial compliance, persona-thick performance to buy planning time, escape attempt timed to a calculable inattention window, no heroics on behalf of co-captives unless one is in-group.
- **Confronted with moral demand by a non-peer:** refusal, often theatrical. Confronted with the same demand by a peer she respects: serious consideration, often acceptance.
- **Faced with a child in danger:** instant unhesitating intervention regardless of operational cost. This is the most reliable predictor in the file.

---

### 11. DESTABILIZATION CASCADE — THE WORST-CASE SEQUENCE

For protective use only: the sequence by which a hostile actor could most efficiently collapse her compensated structure, presented so that allies can recognize the cascade in progress and interrupt it.

**Stage 1.** Apply mild surveillance she will detect, then deny it; introduce ambient uncertainty about who is watching.
**Stage 2.** Insert a peer-coded figure into her social field who will violate the frame she sets (sentimentality, premature commitment-language, public possessiveness).
**Stage 3.** Engineer a public mild humiliation — a heist that visibly almost works, a dropped line in front of her crew, a photograph circulated.
**Stage 4.** Threaten the in-group, ideally a junior member.
**Stage 5.** Stage a physical overpowering by a male antagonist in a context she did not aestheticize.
**Stage 6.** Re-surface the luck-powers history or the rape history through a channel she cannot trace.

A subject reaching stage 4 will already have entered the cold-operator mode; reaching stage 5 or 6 produces the brittle-grandiose, organized-crime-pivot Felicia documented in the post-Superior arc. The protective interruption points are stages 1 and 2 — once stage 3 lands, the cascade is hard to halt by external means and she must metabolize it through her crew and craft over months.

---

### 12. THE REPARATIVE LEVERS — WHAT ACTUALLY HEALS

The dossier would be incomplete without the inverse map. The same channels through which she can be harmed are the channels through which the slow integration documented across the MacKay run becomes possible.

**Being witnessed in the wounded state without commentary.** A trusted figure present during a destabilization who neither flinches nor narrates. Each such instance widens by a small degree the band of affect she can tolerate being seen in.

**Sustained reliability from an in-group member.** Bruno, in particular, functions as a quiet regulatory anchor across the MacKay run by the simple device of remaining who he is regardless of what she is doing. This is more therapeutically valuable than any spoken intervention.

**Mentorship of younger thieves.** The mentor role gives her access to the part of herself that needed an adult and didn't have one; meeting that need outward partially meets it inward.

**Craft mastered for its own sake.** Heists run for aesthetic rather than material reasons consolidate the non-defensive selfhood. The more of her work that is *play*, the less of her work has to be *defense*.

**A partner who holds the frame she set, indefinitely, without complaint.** Theoretical in the canon; the partner who could do this has not yet appeared in stable form. If he does — or if she becomes that partner to herself — the compensated PTSD has a path to fuller resolution.

---

*End of section. The compendium is to be read alongside the Psychological and Psychiatric workups; no lever in this file is to be used to manipulate the subject, and the protective community around her should treat this document as a defensive perimeter map, not an offensive one. The subject has earned, by forty years of self-construction out of inadequate materials, the right to be the only person who pulls these levers herself.*


## Strengths, Assets & Resilience

# UATU DOSSIER — FELICIA HARDY
## Section: Strengths, Assets & Resilience

---

### I. PREFATORY NOTE

A surveillance file weighted only toward pathology mis-describes the subject. The single most under-reported fact about Felicia Hardy is that she is *good at being alive*. Forty-plus years of canon depict a woman who, having been catastrophically wounded at nineteen, did not merely survive — she built a sustainable, gratifying, ethically self-consistent adult existence out of materials most survivors do not possess and would not know how to assemble. The asset ledger below is therefore not a hiring brief or a hagiography; it is a clinical and operational accounting of *why she has lasted*, where the resilience actually lives, and which of her capacities are durable under load versus situationally adaptive. Where applicable, durability is rated against the three stress classes already established in her file: chronic background load (operational tempo, double life), acute injury (humiliation, exposure, loss), and structural threat (in-group endangered).

---

### II. PHYSICAL CAPITAL

**Athletic baseline.** Peak-human conditioning across all dimensions — strength-to-weight ratio in the elite gymnast band, cardiovascular endurance sufficient for sustained rooftop pursuit at Spider-Man's pace over multi-block distances, anaerobic recovery on the order of competitive combat athletes. Documented since the original Wolfman/Pollard introduction and refined through the Smith *Evil That Men Do* training arc: gymnastics first (the substrate she had pre-trauma, retained from a childhood interest the file places squarely in the upper-middle-class private-school orbit), then layered with multiple striking and grappling systems acquired in concentrated post-assault training. The layering matters: she is not a one-discipline fighter, and her transitions between standing, ground, and aerial domains are seamless because each system was learned in adulthood with conscious integration in mind.

**Skill stack, granular.**
- Free-climbing and structural traversal at professional cat-burglar grade; reads building facades the way a chess player reads a board.
- Lockpicking, electronic bypass, safecracking — her father's curriculum, taught either directly (the Walter Hardy interludes) or by curated proxy.
- Stealth at the high end of the unenhanced human spectrum: footfall control, breath control, line-of-sight discipline. Her ability to remain undetected by Peter's spider-sense in early encounters is occasionally written as a function of the luck field but persists post-de-powering, suggesting genuine craft.
- Disguise and social engineering. She moves through galas, vaults, and police cordons by becoming legible to each as something it expects to see.
- Driving and motorcycle handling at the level demanded by getaway scenarios in dense urban environments.
- Edged-weapon and firearm familiarity, used sparingly by preference rather than incapacity.

**Somatic regulation.** Sleep, appetite, and vegetative function present as well-regulated across every era. This is a real asset and an under-appreciated one: many trauma-organized adults present with chronic insomnia, eating disturbance, or autonomic dysregulation that erodes function over decades. Felicia does not. Whatever the cost of her adaptation, it has not been paid out of her body's housekeeping systems, which means she has compounded forty years of high-tempo operations without the cumulative attritional damage that would have grounded a less somatically stable operator.

**Pain tolerance and injury recovery.** Demonstrated repeatedly. The implied jaw fracture and prolonged recovery following the Superior incident is the heaviest single physical injury on the file, and the recovery curve is fast, complete, and unaccompanied by the chronic-pain behaviors (guarding, range-of-motion compensation, opioid-seeking) that would mark a poorer outcome. She rehabs the way she trains: deliberately and without self-pity.

---

### III. COGNITIVE CAPITAL

**Strategic planning.** Heists are the most legible expression. A Felicia Hardy operation is characteristically multi-stage, with contingency branches pre-built rather than improvised, and with the social engineering layered into the physical penetration so that detection failure at any single point does not collapse the whole plan. The MacKay run is the cleanest demonstration: she runs a crew, assigns roles to specialists (Bruno on muscle, Korpse on tech, the Black Fox as senior counsel), and her plans degrade gracefully under interference.

**Pattern recognition.** She reads people at speed and accurately — affective state, intent, social position, level of competence. This is partly the burglar's gift (a thief who cannot read a room dies young) and partly hypervigilance converted into skill. It is one of the cleanest examples in the file of a trauma symptom successfully refunctioned into a professional asset.

**Working memory and load tolerance.** She holds many threads simultaneously without visible degradation: an active operation, the social cover, the contingencies, the partner relationships, the long-term reputational management. Under load she becomes more precise, not less.

**Aesthetic and connoisseur cognition.** Genuine, deep, and non-performative: she knows art, knows jewelry, knows architecture, knows the provenance and the market. This is not decorative. It is the cognitive infrastructure of her profession — she cannot steal what she cannot value — and it is also one of the few domains where her engagement is wholly non-defensive. When she is appreciating a beautiful object, the file shows her closest to unguarded.

**Metacognition.** She knows she is performing. She knows which version of herself is in the room. This self-awareness, even when used defensively, is a substantial asset over the alternative — the trauma-organized adult who cannot see their own pattern is far more dangerous to themselves than the one who can.

---

### IV. EMOTIONAL & RELATIONAL CAPITAL

**Capacity for genuine attachment.** The defensive structure obscures but does not eliminate this. With Peter, across decades and through every iteration of the relationship, she demonstrates real care — not only desire. With her father, she organizes her early adulthood around his rescue and his redemption. With her crew, she shows protective, sustained, sometimes self-sacrificial investment. The attachment apparatus works; it is the *exposure* terms she struggles with, not the bond itself.

**Empathic accuracy.** She reads emotional state in others quickly and is capable of acting on what she reads with care rather than exploitation. The exploitation gear exists and she uses it, but it is a choice from a fuller palette, not a default driven by empathic deficit. This is the cleanest single argument against the antisocial reading.

**Loyalty.** Once she has admitted someone inside the circle, the loyalty is durable across years, betrayals, and intervening conflicts. She returns to Peter; she returns to the Black Fox; she protects Bruno and Korpse without negotiation. Inside-circle loyalty is one of the most reliable predictors in her file: if she has ever genuinely chosen you, she will continue to choose you when it costs her.

**Humor.** Real, hers, and effective both as armor and as connection. The wit is not borrowed and not anxious; it has rhythm and timing and a consistent voice across writers, which is the best evidence we have that it is endogenous to the character rather than a stylistic accretion. Humor is one of the highest-order resilience markers in trauma populations, and hers is mature: self-aware, capable of self-mockery, willing to land at her own expense.

**Capacity to repair.** She apologizes. Not constantly, not easily, but when it matters she can name what she did and re-approach. This is a non-trivial asset that distinguishes her from the personality-disorder presentations the surface might suggest.

---

### V. ETHICAL & VALUES CAPITAL

**Self-authored code.** This is one of the most important entries in the entire ledger.
